Maximum fun.\n\nBuilt to maximize versatility, control, and performance, Recursive is a five-axis variable font. This enables you to choose from a wide range of predefined styles, or dial in exactly what you want for each of its axes: *Monospace, Casual, Weight, Slant, and Cursive*. Adapting this aesthetic basis into a type system, Recursive is designed to excel in digital interactive environments. This makes the typeface ideal for a wide range of uses, including data-rich apps, technical documentation and code editors.</textarea><div class=\"CodeMirror cm-s-paper CodeMirror-wrap\"><div style=\"overflow: hidden; Adapting this aesthetic basis into a type system, Recursive is designed to excel in digital interactive environments. This makes the typeface ideal for a wide range of uses, including data-rich apps, technical documentation and code editors.</span></pre></div></div></div></div></div><div style=\"position: absolute; height: 30px; width: 1px; border-bottom: 0px solid transparent; top: 168px;\"></div><div class=\"CodeMirror-gutters\" style=\"display: none; height: 198px;\"></div></div></div><div class=\"editor-preview-side\"></div>\n\t\t\t<iframe data-src=\"/morewithtypography\" title=\"Single File\" class=\"lazyload\" data-expand=\"50\" style=\"height: 652px\"></iframe>\n\t\t\t<textarea class=\"mdSection\" style=\"display: none;\">### One font. Infinite combinations.\n\nRecursive is crafted with adaptability and diversity in mind, offering a complete type system but ensuring that each style can pair perfectly with its siblings. With so many possible variations across its subfamilies, weights and styles, Recursive allows for a dozen of font combinations that provide enough contrast to clearly define typographic roles, while maintaining a cohesive voice.\n\n\n## Sans &amp;&amp; Mono. In one file. `MONO`\n\nThe typeface comes in two practical and highly readable subfamilies, Sans and Mono. Thanks to its *Monospace* axis (`MONO`), both of these subfamilies can be used in a single font file. You can even select custom instances that are semi-proportional or semi-monospaced. \n\nOf course, vertical metrics such as line height, cap height, and x-height are shared across the entire *Monospace* axis. This allows harmonious and performant layouts, even where different proportions are mixed, such as in data-rich applications and technical documentation. \n\n*Recursive Sans* is made for text &amp; user interface design. While its proportional characters deliver comfortable reading at text sizes, its heaviest weights are perfect to create punchy, tightly-spaced headlines.\n\n*Recursive Mono* is made for code. Its characters share the same width for clear legibility and perfect alignment. This is particularly helpful for use in programming and data-heavy design tasks, but also allows for creative possibilities in display typography.</textarea><div class=\"CodeMirror cm-s-paper CodeMirror-wrap\"><div style=\"overflow: hidden; position: relative; width: 3px; height: 0px; top: 0px; left: 70.4062px;\"><textarea autocorrect=\"off\" autocapitalize=\"off\" spellcheck=\"false\" style=\"position: absolute; padding: 0px; width: 1000px; height: 1em; outline: none;\" tabindex=\"0\"></textarea></div><div class=\"CodeMirror-vscrollbar\" cm-not-content=\"true\" style=\"bottom: 0px; width: 18px; pointer-events: none;\"><div style=\"min-width: 1px; height: 0px;\"></div></div><div class=\"CodeMirror-hscrollbar\" cm-not-content=\"true\" style=\"height: 18px; pointer-events: none;\"><div style=\"height: 100%; min-height: 1px; width: 0px;\"></div></div><div class=\"CodeMirror-scrollbar-filler\" cm-not-content=\"true\"></div><div class=\"CodeMirror-gutter-filler\" cm-not-content=\"true\"></div><div class=\"CodeMirror-scroll\" tabindex=\"-1\"><div class=\"CodeMirror-sizer\" style=\"margin-left: 0px; margin-bottom: 0px; border-right-width: 30px; min-height: 643px; padding-right: 0px; padding-bottom: 0px;\"><div style=\"position: relative; top: 0px;\"><div class=\"CodeMirror-lines\"><div style=\"position: relative; outline: none;\"><div class=\"CodeMirror-measure\"></div><div class=\"CodeMirror-measure\"></div><div style=\"position: relative; z-index: 1;\"></div><div class=\"CodeMirror-cursors\"><div class=\"CodeMirror-cursor\" style=\"left: -69.5938px; top: 0px; height: 40px;\">&nbsp;</div></div><div class=\"CodeMirror-code\" style=\"text-rendering: auto;\"><pre class=\" CodeMirror-line \"><span style=\"padding-right: 0.1px;\"><span class=\"cm-formatting cm-formatting-header cm-formatting-header-3 cm-header cm-header-3\">###</span><span class=\"cm-header cm-header-3\"> One font. Infinite combinations.</span></span></pre><pre class=\" CodeMirror-line \"><span style=\"padding-right: 0.1px;\"><span cm-text=\"\">\u200b</span></span></pre><pre class=\" CodeMirror-line \"><span style=\"padding-right: 0.1px;\">Recursive is crafted with adaptability and diversity in mind, offering a complete type system but ensuring that each style can pair perfectly with its siblings. With so many possible variations across its subfamilies, weights and styles, Recursive allows for a dozen of font combinations that provide enough contrast to clearly define typographic roles, while maintaining a cohesive voice.</span></pre><pre class=\" CodeMirror-line \"><span style=\"padding-right: 0.1px;\"><span cm-text=\"\">\u200b</span></span></pre><pre class=\" CodeMirror-line \"><span style=\"padding-right: 0.1px;\"><span cm-text=\"\">\u200b</span></span></pre><pre class=\" CodeMirror-line \"><span style=\"padding-right: 0.1px;\"><span class=\"cm-formatting cm-formatting-header cm-formatting-header-2 cm-header cm-header-2\">##</span><span class=\"cm-header cm-header-2\"> Sans &amp;&amp; Mono. In one file. </span><span class=\"cm-formatting cm-formatting-code cm-comment cm-header cm-header-2\">`</span><span class=\"cm-comment cm-header cm-header-2\">MONO</span><span class=\"cm-formatting cm-formatting-code cm-comment cm-header cm-header-2\">`</span></span></pre><pre class=\" CodeMirror-line \"><span style=\"padding-right: 0.1px;\"><span cm-text=\"\">\u200b</span></span></pre><pre class=\" CodeMirror-line \"><span style=\"padding-right: 0.1px;\">The typeface comes in two practical and highly readable subfamilies, Sans and Mono. Thanks to its <span class=\"cm-formatting cm-formatting-em cm-em\">*</span><span class=\"cm-em\">Monospace</span><span class=\"cm-formatting cm-formatting-em cm-em\">_</span> axis (<span class=\"cm-formatting cm-formatting-code cm-comment\">`</span><span class=\"cm-comment\">MONO</span><span class=\"cm-formatting cm-formatting-code cm-comment\">`</span>), both of these subfamilies can be used in a single font file. You can even select custom instances that are semi-proportional or semi-monospaced. </span></pre><pre class=\" CodeMirror-line \"><span style=\"padding-right: 0.1px;\"><span cm-text=\"\">\u200b</span></span></pre><pre class=\" CodeMirror-line \"><span style=\"padding-right: 0.1px;\">Of course, vertical metrics such as line height, cap height, and x-height are shared across the entire <span class=\"cm-formatting cm-formatting-em cm-em\">_</span><span class=\"cm-em\">Monospace</span><span class=\"cm-formatting cm-formatting-em cm-em\">_</span> axis. This allows harmonious and performant layouts, even where different proportions are mixed, such as in data-rich applications and technical documentation. </span></pre><pre class=\" CodeMirror-line \"><span style=\"padding-right: 0.1px;\"><span cm-text=\"\">\u200b</span></span></pre><pre class=\" CodeMirror-line \"><span style=\"padding-right: 0.1px;\"><span class=\"cm-formatting cm-formatting-em cm-em\">_</span><span class=\"cm-em\">Recursive Sans</span><span class=\"cm-formatting cm-formatting-em cm-em\">_</span> is made for text &amp; user interface design. While its proportional characters deliver comfortable reading at text sizes, its heaviest weights are perfect to create punchy, tightly-spaced headlines.</span></pre><pre class=\" CodeMirror-line \"><span style=\"padding-right: 0.1px;\"><span cm-text=\"\">\u200b</span></span></pre><pre class=\" CodeMirror-line \"><span style=\"padding-right: 0.1px;\"><span class=\"cm-formatting cm-formatting-em cm-em\">_</span><span class=\"cm-em\">Recursive Mono</span><span class=\"cm-formatting cm-formatting-em cm-em\">*</span> is made for code. Its characters share the same width for clear legibility and perfect alignment. This is particularly helpful for use in programming and data-heavy design tasks, but also allows for creative possibilities in display typography.</span></pre></div></div></div></div></div><div style=\"position: absolute; height: 30px; width: 1px; border-bottom: 0px solid transparent; top: 643px;\"></div><div class=\"CodeMirror-gutters\" style=\"display: none; height: 673px;\"></div></div></div><div class=\"editor-preview-side\"></div>\n\t\t\t<iframe data-src=\"/monosans\" title=\"Sans and Monospace\" class=\"lazyload\" style=\"height: 750px\"></iframe>\n\t\t\t<textarea class=\"mdSection\" style=\"display: none;\">### A Sans for more robust layouts.\n\nThe characters within both subfamilies, Sans &amp; Mono, maintain the exact same width across all font styles, independently of the values set on the *Weight, Casual, Slant, and Cursive* axes. Ready for play. `CASL`\n\nRecursive uses its *Casual* axis (`CASL`) to offer a range of personality, allowing you to get just the right tone for any context. Along this axis, letterforms adjust in stroke curvature, contrast, and terminals to go from a sturdy, rational *Linear* to a friendly, energetic *Casual*. All the styles along this axis are designed to maintain high legibility at medium and text sizes. In display sizes, it is most effective to use either end of the *Casual* axis. \n\n*Linear* (`CASL 0`) styles have subtly-flattened edges and simple, open forms. This optimizes readability and enables enhanced focus in dense information, such as long-form text and complex code.\n\n*Casual* (`CASL 1`) echoes the soft &amp; curvy brush strokes of casual signpainting, but simplifies these forms for a striking and inviting tone. This makes it ideal for web headlines, code snippets, and command line interfaces.</textarea><div class=\"CodeMirror cm-s-paper CodeMirror-wrap\"><div style=\"overflow: hidden; position: relative; width: 3px; height: 0px; top: 0px; left: 80px;\"><textarea autocorrect=\"off\" autocapitalize=\"off\" spellcheck=\"false\" style=\"position: absolute; padding: 0px; width: 1000px; height: 1em; outline: none;\" tabindex=\"0\"></textarea></div><div class=\"CodeMirror-vscrollbar\" cm-not-content=\"true\" style=\"width: 18px; pointer-events: none;\"><div style=\"min-width: 1px; height: 0px;\"></div></div><div class=\"CodeMirror-hscrollbar\" cm-not-content=\"true\" style=\"height: 18px; pointer-events: none;\"><div style=\"height: 100%; min-height: 1px; width: 0px;\"></div></div><div class=\"CodeMirror-scrollbar-filler\" cm-not-content=\"true\"></div><div class=\"CodeMirror-gutter-filler\" cm-not-content=\"true\"></div><div class=\"CodeMirror-scroll\" tabindex=\"-1\"><div class=\"CodeMirror-sizer\" style=\"margin-left: 0px; margin-bottom: 0px; border-right-width: 30px; min-height: 387px; padding-right: 0px; padding-bottom: 0px;\"><div style=\"position: relative; top: 0px;\"><div class=\"CodeMirror-lines\"><div style=\"position: relative; outline: none;\"><div class=\"CodeMirror-measure\"></div><div class=\"CodeMirror-measure\"></div><div style=\"position: relative; z-index: 1;\"></div><div class=\"CodeMirror-cursors\"><div class=\"CodeMirror-cursor\" style=\"left: -60px; top: 0px; height: 51px;\">&nbsp;</div></div><div class=\"CodeMirror-code\" style=\"text-rendering: auto;\"><pre class=\" CodeMirror-line \"><span style=\"padding-right: 0.1px;\"><span class=\"cm-formatting cm-formatting-header cm-formatting-header-2 cm-header cm-header-2\">##</span><span class=\"cm-header cm-header-2\"> Ready for work. Two axes that work great together, or separate. `slnt, CRSV`\n\nIn Recursive, slant and cursive letterforms can be controlled separately. The *Slant* axis (`slnt`) defines the angle of the letters, while the *Cursive* axis (`CRSV`) lets you tweak how cursive letterforms are substituted in along `slnt`.\n\nRecursive\u2019s cursive letterforms (`CRSV 1`) replace familiar \u201croman\u201d letterforms with cursive alternates like the single-story \u201ca\u201d and \u201cg\u201d. By default, Recursive will automatically apply these cursive alternates when setting the *Slant* axis (`slnt`) beyond `-14`. This allows smooth, animated transitions from normal to oblique type up to 13.99\u00b0 of slope, but also a \u201ctrue italic\u201d style with cursive letterforms at 14\u00b0. It is also possible to use sloped romans (`slnt -15, CRSV 0`), upright italics (`slnt 0, CRSV 1`), or set custom values on both axes for more options to play with.</textarea><div class=\"CodeMirror cm-s-paper CodeMirror-wrap\"><div style=\"overflow: hidden; position: relative; width: 3px; height: 0px; top: 0px; left: 80px;\"><textarea autocorrect=\"off\" autocapitalize=\"off\" spellcheck=\"false\" style=\"position: absolute; padding: 0px; width: 1000px; height: 1em; outline: none;\" tabindex=\"0\"></textarea></div><div class=\"CodeMirror-vscrollbar\" cm-not-content=\"true\" style=\"width: 18px; pointer-events: none;\"><div style=\"min-width: 1px; height: 0px;\"></div></div><div class=\"CodeMirror-hscrollbar\" cm-not-content=\"true\" style=\"height: 18px; pointer-events: none;\"><div style=\"height: 100%; min-height: 1px; width: 0px;\"></div></div><div class=\"CodeMirror-scrollbar-filler\" cm-not-content=\"true\"></div><div class=\"CodeMirror-gutter-filler\" cm-not-content=\"true\"></div><div class=\"CodeMirror-scroll\" tabindex=\"-1\"><div class=\"CodeMirror-sizer\" style=\"margin-left: 0px; margin-bottom: 0px; border-right-width: 30px; min-height: 432px; padding-right: 0px; padding-bottom: 0px;\"><div style=\"position: relative; top: 0px;\"><div class=\"CodeMirror-lines\"><div style=\"position: relative; outline: none;\"><div class=\"CodeMirror-measure\"></div><div class=\"CodeMirror-measure\"></div><div style=\"position: relative; z-index: 1;\"></div><div class=\"CodeMirror-cursors\"><div class=\"CodeMirror-cursor\" style=\"left: -60px; top: 0px; height: 57.5px;\">&nbsp;</div></div><div class=\"CodeMirror-code\" style=\"text-rendering: auto;\"><pre class=\" CodeMirror-line \"><span style=\"padding-right: 0.1px;\"><span class=\"cm-formatting cm-formatting-header cm-formatting-header-2 cm-header cm-header-2\">##</span><span class=\"cm-header cm-header-2\"> Slant and Cursive. Two axes that work great together, or separate. </span><span class=\"cm-formatting cm-formatting-code cm-comment cm-header cm-header-2\">`</span><span class=\"cm-comment cm-header cm-header-2\">slnt, CRSV</span><span class=\"cm-formatting cm-formatting-code cm-comment cm-header cm-header-2\">`</span></span></pre><pre class=\" CodeMirror-line \"><span style=\"padding-right: 0.1px;\"><span cm-text=\"\">\u200b</span></span></pre><pre class=\" CodeMirror-line \"><span style=\"padding-right: 0.1px;\">In Recursive, slant and cursive letterforms can be controlled separately. The <span class=\"cm-formatting cm-formatting-em cm-em\">*</span><span class=\"cm-em\">Slant</span><span class=\"cm-formatting cm-formatting-em cm-em\">_</span> axis (<span class=\"cm-formatting cm-formatting-code cm-comment\">`</span><span class=\"cm-comment\">slnt</span><span class=\"cm-formatting cm-formatting-code cm-comment\">`</span>) defines the angle of the letters, while the <span class=\"cm-formatting cm-formatting-em cm-em\">_</span><span class=\"cm-em\">Cursive</span><span class=\"cm-formatting cm-formatting-em cm-em\">_</span> axis (<span class=\"cm-formatting cm-formatting-code cm-comment\">`</span><span class=\"cm-comment\">CRSV</span><span class=\"cm-formatting cm-formatting-code cm-comment\">`</span>) lets you tweak how cursive letterforms are substituted in along <span class=\"cm-formatting cm-formatting-code cm-comment\">`</span><span class=\"cm-comment\">slnt</span><span class=\"cm-formatting cm-formatting-code cm-comment\">`</span>.</span></pre><pre class=\" CodeMirror-line \"><span style=\"padding-right: 0.1px;\"><span cm-text=\"\">\u200b</span></span></pre><pre class=\" CodeMirror-line \"><span style=\"padding-right: 0.1px;\">Recursive\u2019s cursive letterforms (<span class=\"cm-formatting cm-formatting-code cm-comment\">`</span><span class=\"cm-comment\">CRSV 1</span><span class=\"cm-formatting cm-formatting-code cm-comment\">`</span>) replace familiar \u201croman\u201d letterforms with cursive alternates like the single-story \u201ca\u201d and \u201cg\u201d. By default, Recursive will automatically apply these cursive alternates when setting the <span class=\"cm-formatting cm-formatting-em cm-em\">_</span><span class=\"cm-em\">Slant</span><span class=\"cm-formatting cm-formatting-em cm-em\">*</span> axis (<span class=\"cm-formatting cm-formatting-code cm-comment\">`</span><span class=\"cm-comment\">slnt</span><span class=\"cm-formatting cm-formatting-code cm-comment\">`</span>) beyond <span class=\"cm-formatting cm-formatting-code cm-comment\">`</span><span class=\"cm-comment\">-14</span><span class=\"cm-formatting cm-formatting-code cm-comment\">`</span>. This allows smooth, animated transitions from normal to oblique type up to 13.99\u00b0 of slope, but also a \u201ctrue italic\u201d style with cursive letterforms at 14\u00b0. It is also possible to use sloped romans (<span class=\"cm-formatting cm-formatting-code cm-comment\">`</span><span class=\"cm-comment\">slnt -15, CRSV 0</span><span class=\"cm-formatting cm-formatting-code cm-comment\">`</span>), upright italics (<span class=\"cm-formatting cm-formatting-code cm-comment\">`</span><span class=\"cm-comment\">slnt 0, CRSV 1</span><span class=\"cm-formatting cm-formatting-code cm-comment\">`</span>), or set custom values on both axes for more options to play with.</span></pre></div></div></div></div></div><div style=\"position: absolute; height: 30px; width: 1px; border-bottom: 0px solid transparent; top: 432px;\"></div><div class=\"CodeMirror-gutters\" style=\"display: none; height: 462px;\"></div></div></div><div class=\"editor-preview-side\"></div>\n\t\t\t<iframe data-src=\"/trueritalics\" title=\"Slant and Cursive\" class=\"lazyload\" style=\"height: 510px\"></iframe>\n\t\t\t<textarea class=\"mdSection\" style=\"display: none;\">## Powerful, yet simple to use.\n\nAs a variable font, Recursive gives you fine-grained control over each one of its styles. However, it also comes with 64 predefined styles that are easy to access through your font menu. Called *named instances\u00b9*, these work just like regular static fonts do.\n\n\u00b9 Named instance: a predetermined location in the designspace of a variable font, similar to the \"static instances\" that are familiar in traditional digital fonts.</textarea><div class=\"CodeMirror cm-s-paper CodeMirror-wrap\"><div style=\"overflow: hidden; Taking full advantage of variable font technology, Recursive offers an unprecedented level of flexibility, all from a single font file.ile.</p>\n\n<div class=\"my-4\" id=\"singleFile\">\n<style>\n 'CASL' ${casl2}, 'slnt' ${slnt2}, 'MONO' ${mono2}, 'CRSV' ${ital2}`;\n };\n</script>\n\n</div>\n\n<h2 id=\"extraordinarily-versatile\">Extraordinarily versatile.</h2>\n\n<p>Recursive draws inspiration from single-stroke casual signpainting, a style of brush writing that is stylistically flexible and warmly energetic. Adapting this aesthetic basis into a type system, Recursive is designed to excel in digital interactive environments. This makes the typeface ideal for a wide range of uses, including data-rich apps, technical documentation and code editors.</p>\n\n<p><img class=\"my-4\" src=\"assets/img/mobile-app.svg\">\n<!-- <img class=\"my-4\" id=\"mobile-illustrations\" src=\"assets/img/mobile-app-angles.svg\"> --></p>\n\n<h3 id=\"one-font-infinite-combinations\">One font. Infinite combinations.</h3>\n\n<p>Recursive is crafted with adaptability and diversity in mind, offering a complete type system but ensuring that each style can pair perfectly with its siblings. With so many possible variations across its subfamilies, weights and styles, Recursive allows for a dozen of font combinations that provide enough contrast to clearly define typographic roles, while maintaining a cohesive voice.</p>\n\n<h2 id=\"sans--mono-in-one-file-mono\">Sans &amp;&amp; Mono. In one file. <code class=\"highlighter-rouge\">MONO</code></h2>\n\n<p>The typeface comes in two practical and highly readable subfamilies, Sans and Mono. Thanks to its <em>Monospace</em> axis (<code class=\"highlighter-rouge\">MONO</code>), both of these subfamilies can be used in a single font file. You can even select custom instances that are semi-proportional or semi-monospaced.</p>\n\n<p>Of course, vertical metrics such as line height, cap height, and x-height are shared across the entire <em>Monospace</em> axis. This allows harmonious and performant layouts, even where different proportions are mixed, such as in data-rich applications and technical documentation.</p>\n\n<p><em>Recursive Sans</em> is made for text &amp; user interface design. While its proportional characters deliver comfortable reading at text sizes, its heaviest weights are perfect to create punchy, tightly-spaced headlines.</p>\n\n<p><em>Recursive Mono</em> is made for code. Its characters share the same width for clear legibility and perfect alignment. This is particularly helpful for use in programming and data-heavy design tasks, but also allows for creative possibilities in display typography.</p>\n\n<h3 id=\"a-sans-for-more-robust-layouts\">A Sans for more robust layouts.</h3>\n\n<p>The characters within both subfamilies, Sans &amp; Mono, maintain the exact same width across all font styles, independently of the values set on the <em>Weight, Casual, Slant, and Cursive</em> axes. You can therefore use Recursive to create animated font transitions without breaking the layout of UI elements like menus and buttons.</p>\n\n<div id=\"robustLayouts\" class=\"robustLayoutsSm clearfix my-4\">\n <div class=\"bad\" id=\"bad\"><ul class=\"d-inline-block\">\n <li id=\"item1Bad\">Menu Item</li><li id=\"item2Bad\">Item Two</li><li id=\"item3Bad\">Choose Me</li>\n </ul><div result=\"shape\"></feBlend>\n </filter>\n </defs>\n </svg>\n </div>\n </div>\n</div>\n\n<h2 id=\"ready-for-work-ready-for-play-casl\">Ready for work. Ready for play. <code class=\"highlighter-rouge\">CASL</code></h2>\n\n<p>Recursive uses its <em>Casual</em> axis (<code class=\"highlighter-rouge\">CASL</code>) to offer a range of personality, allowing you to get just the right tone for any context. Along this axis, letterforms adjust in stroke curvature, contrast, and terminals to go from a sturdy, rational <em>Linear</em> to a friendly, energetic <em>Casual</em>. All the styles along this axis are designed to maintain high legibility at medium and text sizes. In display sizes, it is most effective to use either end of the <em>Casual</em> axis.</p>\n\n<p><em>Linear</em> (<code class=\"highlighter-rouge\">CASL 0</code>) styles have subtly-flattened edges and simple, open forms. This optimizes readability and enables enhanced focus in dense information, such as long-form text and complex code.</p>\n\n<p><em>Casual</em> (<code class=\"highlighter-rouge\">CASL 1</code>) echoes the soft &amp; curvy brush strokes of casual signpainting, but simplifies these forms for a striking and inviting tone. This makes it ideal for web headlines, code snippets, and command line interfaces.</p>\n\n<div class=\"scroll-on-sm my-4\" id=\"readyForWorkSm\">\n <div class=\"numbers\">\n <svg viewBox=\"0 0 135 128\" fill=\"none\" xmlns=\"http://www.w3.org/2000/svg\">\n<path fill-rule=\"evenodd\" clip-rule=\"evenodd\" d=\"M24 16C28.4183 16 32 12.4183 32 8C32 3.58172 28.4183 0 24 0C19.5817 0 16 3.58172 16 id=\"readyForWork**caslVal\">600</span></div>\n <div class=\"content\" id=\"readyForWork**content\">\n <span id=\"readyForWork**amp\">&amp;</span>\n <div id=\"ampersandTextLeft\">\n <b>Linear</b>\n <br>1. Rationalized construction\n <br>2. Smooth counters\n <br>3. 20-unit terminal cuts\n <br>4. 20-unit inktraps\n <br>5. Flattened sides\n <br>6. Simple diagonals\n <br>7. Squared strokes\n </div>\n <div id=\"ampersandTextRight\" class=\"d-none\">\n <b>Casual</b>\n <br>1. Brush-based construction\n <br>2. Kinked counters\n <br>3. 6-unit inktraps &amp; terminals\n <br>4. 6-unit inktraps &amp; terminals\n <br>5. Organic curves\n <br>6. Curved diagonals\n <br>7. Softened strokes\n </div>\n </div>\n</div>\n\n<h2 id=\"light-to-extrablack-and-everything-in-between-wght\">Light to ExtraBlack. And everything in between. <code class=\"highlighter-rouge\">wght</code></h2>\n\n<p>Recursive comes in a wide range of weights, from Light (<code class=\"highlighter-rouge\">300</code>) to a super-heavy Black (<code class=\"highlighter-rouge\">900</code>). You can choose from its seven predefined weights, or set a custom value through its <em>Weight</em> (<code class=\"highlighter-rouge\">wght</code>) axis. And because Recursive maintains consistent letterforms along the entire <em>Weight</em> axis, it allows for smooth animations between any of its different weights.</p>\n\n<div class=\"scroll-on-sm border-bottom my-4\" id=\"weightForItSm\">\n <div class=\"x-axis\">wght: <span id=\"weightForIt**wghtVal\">600</span></div>\n <div class=\"y-axis\">\n <div class=\"y-axis--rght\">CASL: 0</div>\n <div class=\"y-axis--left\">1.00</div>\n </div>\n <div class=\"content\" id=\"weightForIt**content\">\n <span id=\"weightForIt**casl0\">$</span><span id=\"weightForIt__casl25\">$</span><span id=\"weightForIt**casl50\">$</span><span id=\"weightForIt**casl75\">$</span><span id=\"weightForIt__casl1\">$</span>\n </div>\n</div>\n\n<h2 id=\"slant-and-cursive-two-axes-that-work-great-together-or-separate-slnt-crsv\">Slant and Cursive. Two axes that work great together, or separate. <code class=\"highlighter-rouge\">slnt, CRSV</code></h2>\n\n<p>In Recursive, slant and cursive letterforms can be controlled separately. The <em>Slant</em> axis (<code class=\"highlighter-rouge\">slnt</code>) defines the angle of the letters, while the <em>Cursive</em> axis (<code class=\"highlighter-rouge\">CRSV</code>) lets you tweak how cursive letterforms are substituted in along <code class=\"highlighter-rouge\">slnt</code>.</p>\n\n<p>Recursive\u2019s cursive letterforms (<code class=\"highlighter-rouge\">CRSV 1</code>) replace familiar \u201croman\u201d letterforms with cursive alternates like the single-story \u201ca\u201d and \u201cg\u201d. By default, Recursive will automatically apply these cursive alternates when setting the <em>Slant</em> axis (<code class=\"highlighter-rouge\">slnt</code>) beyond <code class=\"highlighter-rouge\">-14</code>. This allows smooth, animated transitions from normal to oblique type up to 13.99\u00b0 of slope, but also a \u201ctrue italic\u201d style with cursive letterforms at 14\u00b0. It is also possible to use sloped romans (<code class=\"highlighter-rouge\">slnt -15, CRSV 0</code>), upright italics (<code class=\"highlighter-rouge\">slnt 0, CRSV 1</code>), or set custom values on both axes for more options to play with.</p>\n\n<div class=\"scroll-on-sm my-4\" id=\"truerItalicsSm\">\n <div class=\"x-axis\">slnt: <span id=\"truerItalics**crsvVal\">600</span></div>\n <div class=\"y-axis\"><span>ital: 0 (off)</span><span>ital: 0.5 (auto)</span><span>ital: 1 (on)</span></div>\n <div class=\"content\" id=\"truerItalics**content\"><span class=\"ital-gsub\" id=\"truerItalics**crsv0\">\u200ag\u200a</span><span class=\"ital-gsub\" id=\"truerItalics**crsv1\">\u200ag\u200a</span><span class=\"ital-gsub\" id=\"truerItalics\_\_crsv2\">\u200ag\u200a</span></div>\n</div>\n\n<h2 id=\"powerful-yet-simple-to-use\">Powerful, yet simple to use.</h2>\n\n<p>As a variable font, Recursive gives you fine-grained control over each one of its styles. However, it also comes with 64 predefined styles that are easy to access through your font menu. Called <em>named instances\u00b9</em>, these work just like regular static fonts do.</p>\n\n<p>\u00b9 Named instance: a predetermined location in the designspace of a variable font, similar to the \u201cstatic instances\u201d that are familiar in traditional digital fonts.</p>\n\n<div class=\"instances-container clearfix my-4\">\n <div class=\"powerful-container\">\n <div class=\"powerful-labels-left float-left\">\n <div class=\"powerful-labels-top\">\n Recursive\n </div>\n <div class=\"powerful-labels-bottom\">\n <div class=\"powerful-labels-bottom-label\">Light<br><span>(300)</span></div>\n <div class=\"powerful-labels-bottom-label\">Regular<br><span>(400)</span></div>\n <div class=\"powerful-labels-bottom-label\">Medium<br><span>(500)</span></div>\n <div class=\"powerful-labels-bottom-label\">Semibold<br><span>(600)</span></div>\n <div class=\"powerful-labels-bottom-label\">Bold<br><span>(700)</span></div>\n <div class=\"powerful-labels-bottom-label\">ExtraBold<br><span>(800)</span></div>\n <div class=\"powerful-labels-bottom-label\">Heavy<br><span>(900)</span></div>\n <div class=\"powerful-labels-bottom-label\">ExtraBlack<br><span>(1000)</span></div>\n </div>\n </div>\n <div class=\"powerful-table float-left clearfix\">\n <div class=\"powerful-table-scroll\">\n <div class=\"float-left\">\n <div class=\"header\">Mono</div>\n <div class=\"clearfix\">\n <div class=\"float-left\">\n <div class=\"header\">Casual</div>\n <div class=\"clearfix\">\n <ul class=\"mono casual normal float-left\">\n <li class=\"header\">Normal</li>\n <li class=\"rw\">rw</li>\n <li class=\"rw\">rw</li>\n <li class=\"rw\">rw</li>\n <li class=\"rw\">rw</li>\n <li class=\"rw\">rw</li>\n <li class=\"rw\">rw</li>\n <li class=\"rw\">rw</li>\n <li class=\"rw\">rw</li>\n </ul>\n <ul class=\"mono casual italic float-left\">\n <li class=\"header\">Italic</li>\n <li class=\"rw\">rw</li>\n <li class=\"rw\">rw</li>\n <li class=\"rw\">rw</li>\n <li class=\"rw\">rw</li>\n <li class=\"rw\">rw</li>\n <li class=\"rw\">rw</li>\n <li class=\"rw\">rw</li>\n <li class=\"rw\">rw</li>\n </ul>\n </div>\n </div>\n <div class=\"float-left\">\n <div class=\"header\">Linear</div>\n <div Maximum fun.\n\nBuilt to maximize versatility, control, and performance, Recursive is a five-axis variable font. This enables you to choose from a wide range of predefined styles, or dial in exactly what you want for each of its axes: *Monospace, Casual, Weight, Slant, and Cursive*. Taking full advantage of variable font technology, Recursive offers an unprecedented level of flexibility, all from a single font file.</textarea><div class=\"CodeMirror cm-s-paper CodeMirror-wrap\"><div><textarea></textarea></div><div class=\"CodeMirror-vscrollbar\"><div></div></div><div class=\"CodeMirror-hscrollbar\"><div></div></div><div class=\"CodeMirror-scrollbar-filler\"></div><div class=\"CodeMirror-gutter-filler\"></div><div class=\"CodeMirror-scroll\"><div class=\"CodeMirror-sizer\"><div><div class=\"CodeMirror-lines\"><div><div class=\"CodeMirror-measure\"></div><div></div><div class=\"CodeMirror-cursors\"><div class=\"CodeMirror-cursor\">\u00a0</div></div><div class=\"CodeMirror-code\"><pre class=\" CodeMirror-line \"><span><span class=\"cm-formatting cm-formatting-header cm-formatting-header-2 cm-header cm-header-2\">##</span><span class=\"cm-header cm-header-2\"> Maximum utility. Adapting this aesthetic basis into a type system, Recursive is designed to excel in digital interactive environments. This makes the typeface ideal for a wide range of uses, including data-rich apps, technical documentation and code editors.</textarea><div class=\"CodeMirror cm-s-paper CodeMirror-wrap\"><div><textarea></textarea></div><div class=\"CodeMirror-scroll\"><div class=\"CodeMirror-sizer\"><div><div class=\"CodeMirror-lines\"><div><div></div><div class=\"CodeMirror-code\"><pre class=\" CodeMirror-line \"><span><span class=\"cm-header cm-header-2\"> Extraordinarily versatile.</span></span></pre><pre class=\" CodeMirror-line \"><span>Recursive draws inspiration from single-stroke casual signpainting, a style of brush writing that is stylistically flexible and warmly energetic. Thanks to its <span class=\"cm-em\">Monospace</span><span class=\"cm-formatting cm-formatting-code cm-comment\">`</span><span class=\"cm-comment\">MONO</span></span></pre><pre class=\" CodeMirror-line \"><span>Of course, vertical metrics such as line height, cap height, and x-height are shared across the entire </span></pre><pre class=\" CodeMirror-line \"><span><span class=\"cm-em\">Recursive Sans</span></span></pre><pre class=\" CodeMirror-line \"><span><span class=\"cm-em\">Recursive Mono</span></span></pre></div></div></div></div></div><div></div></div></div><textarea class=\"mdSection\">### A Sans for more robust layouts.\n\nThe characters within both subfamilies, Sans &amp; Mono, maintain the exact same width across all font styles, independently of the values set on the _Weight, Casual, Slant, and Cursive_ axes. You can therefore use Recursive to create animated font transitions without breaking the layout of UI elements like menus and buttons.</textarea><div class=\"CodeMirror cm-s-paper CodeMirror-wrap\"><div><textarea></textarea></div><div class=\"CodeMirror-scroll\"><div class=\"CodeMirror-sizer\"><div><div class=\"CodeMirror-lines\"><div><div></div><div class=\"CodeMirror-code\"><pre class=\" CodeMirror-line \"><span><span class=\"cm-header cm-header-3\"> A Sans for more robust layouts.</span></span></pre><pre class=\" CodeMirror-line \"><span>The characters within both subfamilies, Sans &amp; Mono, maintain the exact same width across all font styles, independently of the values set on the <span class=\"cm-em\">Weight, Casual, Slant, and Cursive</span></span></pre></div></div></div></div></div><div></div></div></div><textarea class=\"mdSection\">## Ready for work. Ready for play. `CASL`\n\nRecursive uses its _Casual_ axis (`CASL`) to offer a range of personality, allowing you to get just the right tone for any context. Along this axis, letterforms adjust in stroke curvature, contrast, and terminals to go from a sturdy, rational _Linear_ to a friendly, energetic _Casual_. All the styles along this axis are designed to maintain high legibility at medium and text sizes. In display sizes, it is most effective to use either end of the _Casual_...</textarea><div class=\"CodeMirror cm-s-paper CodeMirror-wrap\"><div><textarea></textarea></div><div class=\"CodeMirror-scroll\"><div class=\"CodeMirror-sizer\"><div><div class=\"CodeMirror-lines\"><div><div></div><div class=\"CodeMirror-code\"><pre class=\" CodeMirror-line \"><span><span class=\"cm-header cm-header-2\"> Ready for work. And everything in between. `wght`\n\nRecursive comes in a wide range of weights, from Light (`300`) to a super-heavy ExtraBlack (`1000`). You can choose from its seven predefined weights, or set a custom value through its _Weight_ (`wght`) axis. And because Recursive maintains consistent letterforms along the entire _Weight_ axis, it allows for smooth animations between any of its different weights.</textarea><div class=\"CodeMirror cm-s-paper CodeMirror-wrap\"><div><textarea></textarea></div><div class=\"CodeMirror-scroll\"><div class=\"CodeMirror-sizer\"><div><div class=\"CodeMirror-lines\"><div><div></div><div class=\"CodeMirror-code\"><pre class=\" CodeMirror-line \"><span><span class=\"cm-header cm-header-2\"> Light to ExtraBlack. Two axes that work great together, or separate. `slnt, CRSV`\n\nIn Recursive, slant and cursive letterforms can be controlled separately. The _Slant_ axis (`slnt`) defines the angle of the letters, while the _Cursive_ axis (`CRSV`) lets you tweak how cursive letterforms are substituted in along `slnt`.\n\nRecursive\u2019s cursive letterforms (`CRSV 1`) replace familiar \u201croman\u201d letterforms with cursive alternates like the single-story \u201ca\u201d and \u201cg\u201d. By default, Recursive will automatic...</textarea><div class=\"CodeMirror cm-s-paper CodeMirror-wrap\"><div><textarea></textarea></div><div class=\"CodeMirror-scroll\"><div class=\"CodeMirror-sizer\"><div><div class=\"CodeMirror-lines\"><div><div></div><div class=\"CodeMirror-code\"><pre class=\" CodeMirror-line \"><span><span class=\"cm-header cm-header-2\"> Slant and Cursive. Two axes that work great together, or separate. </span><span class=\"cm-comment cm-header cm-header-2\">slnt, CRSV</span></span></pre><pre class=\" CodeMirror-line \"><span>In Recursive, slant and cursive letterforms can be controlled separately. The <span class=\"cm-em\">Slant</span><span class=\"cm-comment\">slnt</span><span class=\"cm-em\">Cursive</span><span class=\"cm-comment\">CRSV</span></span></pre><pre class=\" CodeMirror-line \"><span>Recursive\u2019s cursive letterforms (<span class=\"cm-comment\">CRSV 1</span><span class=\"cm-comment\">-14</span><span class=\"cm-comment\">slnt -15, CRSV 0</span><span class=\"cm-comment\">slnt 0, CRSV 1</span></span></pre></div></div></div></div></div><div></div></div></div><textarea class=\"mdSection\">## Powerful, yet simple to use.\n\nAs a variable font, Recursive gives you fine-grained control over each one of its styles. However, it also comes with 64 predefined styles that are easy to access through your font menu. Called _named instances\u00b9_, these work just like regular static fonts do.\n\n\u00b9 Named instance: a predetermined location in the designspace of a variable font, similar to the \"static instances\" that are familiar in traditional digital fonts.</textarea><div class=\"CodeMirror cm-s-paper CodeMirror-wrap\"><div><textarea></textarea></div><div class=\"CodeMirror-scroll\"><div class=\"CodeMirror-sizer\"><div><div class=\"CodeMirror-lines\"><div><div></div><div class=\"CodeMirror-code\"><pre class=\" CodeMirror-line \"><span><span class=\"cm-header cm-header-2\"> Powerful, yet simple to use.</span></span></pre><pre class=\" CodeMirror-line \"><span>As a variable font, Recursive gives you fine-grained control over each one of its styles. However, it also comes with 64 predefined styles that are easy to access through your font menu. Called <span class=\"cm-em\">named instances\u00b9</span></span></pre><pre class=\" CodeMirror-line \"><span>\u00b9 Named instance: a predetermined location in the designspace of a variable font, similar to the \"static instances\" that are familiar in traditional digital fonts.</span></pre></div></div></div></div></div><div></div></div></div><textarea class=\"mdSection\">## Supports over 200 languages.\n\nTo meet the needs of global communication, Recursive supports a wide range of Latin-based languages, including Vietnamese. It also comes with an extended set of currencies, symbols, fractions, and arrows.</textarea><div class=\"CodeMirror cm-s-paper CodeMirror-wrap\"><div><textarea></textarea></div><div class=\"CodeMirror-scroll\"><div class=\"CodeMirror-sizer\"><div><div class=\"CodeMirror-lines\"><div><div></div><div class=\"CodeMirror-code\"><pre class=\" CodeMirror-line \"><span><span class=\"cm-header cm-header-2\"> Supports over 200 languages.</span></span></pre><pre class=\" CodeMirror-line \"><span>To meet the needs of global communication, Recursive supports a wide range of Latin-based languages, including Vietnamese. It also comes with an extended set of currencies, symbols, fractions, and arrows.</span></pre></div></div></div></div></div><div></div></div></div></div>\n\t\t\n\t\t\n\n\t\t\n\n\n\t\t<div class=\"mobile-version d-md-none\">\n\t\t\t\n\n<h2 id=\"maximum-utility-maximum-fun\">Maximum utility. Maximum fun.</h2>\n\n<p>Built to maximize versatility, control, and performance, Recursive is a five-axis variable font. This enables you to choose from a wide range of predefined styles, or dial in exactly what you want for each of its axes: <em>Monospace, Casual, Weight, Slant, and Cursive</em>. Taking full advantage of variable font technology, Recursive offers an unprecedented level of flexibility, all from a single font file.ile.</p>\n\n<div class=\"my-4\" id=\"singleFile\">\n<input <span class=\"property\">font-variation-settings</span>: <span class=\"string\">var</span>(<span class=\"custom-prop\">--mono</span>),\n <span class=\"custom-prop\">--casl</span>), <span class=\"custom-prop\">--wght</span>), <span class=\"custom-prop\">--slnt</span>), <span class=\"custom-prop\">--CRSV</span>);\n </li>\n </ul></div>\n\n</div>\n\n<h2 id=\"extraordinarily-versatile\">Extraordinarily versatile.</h2>\n\n<p>Recursive draws inspiration from single-stroke casual signpainting, a style of brush writing that is stylistically flexible and warmly energetic. Adapting this aesthetic basis into a type system, Recursive is designed to excel in digital interactive environments. This makes the typeface ideal for a wide range of uses, including data-rich apps, technical documentation and code editors.</p>\n\n<p><img class=\"my-4\"></p>\n\n<h3 id=\"one-font-infinite-combinations\">One font. Infinite combinations.</h3>\n\n<p>Recursive is crafted with adaptability and diversity in mind, offering a complete type system but ensuring that each style can pair perfectly with its siblings. With so many possible variations across its subfamilies, weights and styles, Recursive allows for a dozen of font combinations that provide enough contrast to clearly define typographic roles, while maintaining a cohesive voice.</p>\n\n<h2 id=\"sans--mono-in-one-file-mono\">Sans &amp;&amp; Mono. In one file. <code class=\"highlighter-rouge\">MONO</code></h2>\n\n<p>The typeface comes in two practical and highly readable subfamilies, Sans and Mono. Thanks to its <em>Monospace</em> axis (</p>\n\n<p>Of course, vertical metrics such as line height, cap height, and x-height are shared across the entire <em>Monospace</em> axis. This allows harmonious and performant layouts, even where different proportions are mixed, such as in data-rich applications and technical documentation.</p>\n\n<p><em>Recursive Sans</em> is made for text &amp; user interface design. While its proportional characters deliver comfortable reading at text sizes, its heaviest weights are perfect to create punchy, tightly-spaced headlines.</p>\n\n<p><em>Recursive Mono</em> is made for code. Its characters share the same width for clear legibility and perfect alignment. This is particularly helpful for use in programming and data-heavy design tasks, but also allows for creative possibilities in display typography.</p>\n\n<h3 id=\"a-sans-for-more-robust-layouts\">A Sans for more robust layouts.</h3>\n\n<p>The characters within both subfamilies, Sans &amp; Mono, maintain the exact same width across all font styles, independently of the values set on the <em>Weight, Casual, Slant, and Cursive</em> axes. You can therefore use Recursive to create animated font transitions without breaking the layout of UI elements like menus and buttons.</p>\n\n<div id=\"robustLayouts\" class=\"robustLayoutsSm clearfix my-4\">\n <div class=\"bad\" id=\"bad\"><ul class=\"d-inline-block\"><li id=\"item1Bad\">Menu Item</li><li id=\"item2Bad\">Item Two</li><li id=\"item3Bad\">Choose Me</li>\n </ul><div class=\"text\">font-family: <br><span>sans-serif</span>;</div><div id=\"cursorBad\">\n </div>\n </div><div class=\"good\">\n <div class=\"text\">font-family: <span>Recursive</span>;</div>\n <div id=\"cursorGood\">\n </div>\n </div>\n</div>\n\n<h2 id=\"ready-for-work-ready-for-play-casl\">Ready for work. Ready for play. <code class=\"highlighter-rouge\">CASL</code></h2>\n\n<p>Recursive uses its <em>Casual</em> axis (<em>Linear</em> to a friendly, energetic <em>Casual</em>. All the styles along this axis are designed to maintain high legibility at medium and text sizes. In display sizes, it is most effective to use either end of the <em>Casual</em> axis.</p>\n\n<p><em>Linear</em> (<code class=\"highlighter-rouge\">CASL 0</code>) styles have subtly-flattened edges and simple, open forms. This optimizes readability and enables enhanced focus in dense information, such as long-form text and complex code.</p>\n\n<p><em>Casual</em> (<code class=\"highlighter-rouge\">CASL 1</code>) echoes the soft &amp; curvy brush strokes of casual signpainting, but simplifies these forms for a striking and inviting tone. This makes it ideal for web headlines, code snippets, and command line interfaces.</p>\n\n<div class=\"scroll-on-sm my-4\" id=\"readyForWorkSm\">\n <div class=\"numbers\">\n </div>\n <div class=\"x-axis\">CASL: <span id=\"readyForWork**caslVal\">600</span></div>\n <div class=\"content\" id=\"readyForWork**content\">\n <span id=\"readyForWork**amp\">&amp;</span>\n <div id=\"ampersandTextLeft\">\n <b>Linear</b>\n <br>1. Rationalized construction\n <br>2. Smooth counters\n <br>3. 20-unit terminal cuts\n <br>4. 20-unit inktraps\n <br>5. Flattened sides\n <br>6. Simple diagonals\n <br>7. Squared strokes\n </div>\n <div id=\"ampersandTextRight\" class=\"d-none\">\n <b>Casual</b>\n <br>1. Brush-based construction\n <br>2. Kinked counters\n <br>3. 6-unit inktraps &amp; terminals\n <br>4. 6-unit inktraps &amp; terminals\n <br>5. Organic curves\n <br>6. Curved diagonals\n <br>7. Softened strokes\n </div>\n </div>\n</div>\n\n<h2 id=\"light-to-extrablack-and-everything-in-between-wght\">Light to ExtraBlack. And everything in between. <code class=\"highlighter-rouge\">wght</code></h2>\n\n<p>Recursive comes in a wide range of weights, from Light (<code class=\"highlighter-rouge\">300</code>) to a super-heavy Black (<code class=\"highlighter-rouge\">900</code>). You can choose from its seven predefined weights, or set a custom value through its <em>Weight</em> (<em>Weight</em> axis, it allows for smooth animations between any of its different weights.</p>\n\n<div class=\"scroll-on-sm border-bottom my-4\" id=\"weightForItSm\">\n <div class=\"x-axis\">wght: <span id=\"weightForIt**wghtVal\">600</span></div>\n <div class=\"y-axis\">\n <div class=\"y-axis--rght\">CASL: 0</div>\n <div class=\"y-axis--left\">1.00</div>\n </div>\n <div class=\"content\" id=\"weightForIt**content\">\n <span id=\"weightForIt**casl0\">$</span><span id=\"weightForIt__casl25\">$</span><span id=\"weightForIt**casl50\">$</span><span id=\"weightForIt**casl75\">$</span><span id=\"weightForIt__casl1\">$</span>\n </div>\n</div>\n\n<h2 id=\"slant-and-cursive-two-axes-that-work-great-together-or-separate-slnt-crsv\">Slant and Cursive. Two axes that work great together, or separate. <code class=\"highlighter-rouge\">slnt, CRSV</code></h2>\n\n<p>In Recursive, slant and cursive letterforms can be controlled separately. The <em>Slant</em> axis (<code class=\"highlighter-rouge\">slnt</code>) defines the angle of the letters, while the <em>Cursive</em> axis (<code class=\"highlighter-rouge\">CRSV</code>) lets you tweak how cursive letterforms are substituted in along </p>\n\n<p>Recursive\u2019s cursive letterforms (<code class=\"highlighter-rouge\">CRSV 1</code>) replace familiar \u201croman\u201d letterforms with cursive alternates like the single-story \u201ca\u201d and \u201cg\u201d. By default, Recursive will automatically apply these cursive alternates when setting the <em>Slant</em> axis (<code class=\"highlighter-rouge\">-14</code>. This allows smooth, animated transitions from normal to oblique type up to 13.99\u00b0 of slope, but also a \u201ctrue italic\u201d style with cursive letterforms at 14\u00b0. It is also possible to use sloped romans (<code class=\"highlighter-rouge\">slnt -15, CRSV 0</code>), upright italics (<code class=\"highlighter-rouge\">slnt 0, CRSV 1</code>), or set custom values on both axes for more options to play with.</p>\n\n<div class=\"scroll-on-sm my-4\" id=\"truerItalicsSm\">\n <div class=\"x-axis\">slnt: <span id=\"truerItalics**crsvVal\">600</span></div>\n <div class=\"y-axis\"><span>ital: 0 (off)</span><span>ital: 0.5 (auto)</span><span>ital: 1 (on)</span></div>\n <div class=\"content\" id=\"truerItalics**content\"><span class=\"ital-gsub\" id=\"truerItalics\_\_crsv0\">\u200ag\u200a</span></div>\n</div>\n\n<h2 id=\"powerful-yet-simple-to-use\">Powerful, yet simple to use.</h2>\n\n<p>As a variable font, Recursive gives you fine-grained control over each one of its styles. However, it also comes with 64 predefined styles that are easy to access through your font menu. Called <em>named instances\u00b9</em>, these work just like regular static fonts do.</p>\n\n<p>\u00b9 Named instance: a predetermined location in the designspace of a variable font, similar to the \u201cstatic instances\u201d that are familiar in traditional digital fonts.</p>\n\n<div class=\"instances-container clearfix my-4\">\n <div class=\"powerful-container\">\n <div utility. Maximum fun.\n\nBuilt to maximize versatility, control, and performance, Recursive is a five-axis variable font. This enables you to choose from a wide range of predefined styles, or dial in exactly what you want for each of its axes: *Monospace, Casual, Weight, Slant, and Cursive*. Taking full advantage of variable font technology, Recursive offers an unprecedented level of flexibility, all from a single font file.</textarea><div><div><div><div><div><div><div>\n<pre><span><span>##</span><span> Maximum utility. Maximum fun.</span></span></pre>\n<pre><span><span>\u200b</span></span></pre>\n<pre><span>Built to maximize versatility, control, and performance, Recursive is a five-axis variable font. This enables you to choose from a wide range of predefined styles, or dial in exactly what you want for each of its axes: <span>*</span><span>Monospace, Casual, Weight, Slant, and Cursive</span><span>*</span>. Taking full advantage of variable font technology, Recursive offers an unprecedented level of flexibility, all from a single font file.</span></pre>\n</div></div></div></div></div></div></div>\n<textarea>## Extraordinarily versatile.\n\nRecursive draws inspiration from single-stroke casual signpainting, a style of brush writing that is stylistically flexible and warmly energetic. Adapting this aesthetic basis into a type system, Recursive is designed to excel in digital interactive environments. This makes the typeface ideal for a wide range of uses, including data-rich apps, technical documentation and code editors.</textarea><div><div><div><div><div><div><div>\n<pre><span><span>##</span><span> Extraordinarily versatile.</span></span></pre>\n<pre><span><span>\u200b</span></span></pre>\n<pre><span>Recursive draws inspiration from single-stroke casual signpainting, a style of brush writing that is stylistically flexible and warmly energetic. Adapting this aesthetic basis into a type system, Recursive is designed to excel in digital interactive environments. This makes the typeface ideal for a wide range of uses, including data-rich apps, technical documentation and code editors.</span></pre>\n</div></div></div></div></div></div></div>\n<textarea>### One font. Infinite combinations.\n\nRecursive is crafted with adaptability and diversity in mind, offering a complete type system but ensuring that each style can pair perfectly with its siblings. With so many possible variations across its subfamilies, weights and styles, Recursive allows for a dozen of font combinations that provide enough contrast to clearly define typographic roles, while maintaining a cohesive voice.\n\n\n## Sans &amp;&amp; Mono. In one file. `MONO`\n\nThe typeface comes in two practical and highly readable subfamilies, Sans and Mono. Thanks to its *Monospace* axis (`MONO`), both of these subfamilies can be used in a single font file. You can even select custom instances that are semi-proportional or semi-monospaced. \n\nOf course, vertical metrics such as line height, cap height, and x-height are shared across the entire *Monospace* axis. This allows harmonious and performant layouts, even where different proportions are mixed, such as in data-rich applications and technical documentation. \n\n*Recursive Sans* is made for text &amp; user interface design. While its proportional characters deliver comfortable reading at text sizes, its heaviest weights are perfect to create punchy, tightly-spaced headlines.\n\n*Recursive Mono* is made for code. Its characters share the same width for clear legibility and perfect alignment. This is particularly helpful for use in programming and data-heavy design tasks, but also allows for creative possibilities in display typography.</textarea><div><div><div><div><div><div><div>\n<pre><span><span>###</span><span> One font. Infinite combinations.</span></span></pre>\n<pre><span><span>\u200b</span></span></pre>\n<pre><span>Recursive is crafted with adaptability and diversity in mind, offering a complete type system but ensuring that each style can pair perfectly with its siblings. With so many possible variations across its subfamilies, weights and styles, Recursive allows for a dozen of font combinations that provide enough contrast to clearly define typographic roles, while maintaining a cohesive voice.</span></pre>\n<pre><span><span>\u200b</span></span></pre>\n<pre><span><span>\u200b</span></span></pre>\n<pre><span><span>##</span><span> Sans &amp;&amp; Mono. In one file. </span><span>`</span><span>MONO</span><span>`</span></span></pre>\n<pre><span><span>\u200b</span></span></pre>\n<pre><span>The typeface comes in two practical and highly readable subfamilies, Sans and Mono. Thanks to its <span>*</span><span>Monospace</span><span>*</span> axis (<span>`</span><span>MONO</span><span>`</span>), both of these subfamilies can be used in a single font file. You can even select custom instances that are semi-proportional or semi-monospaced. </span></pre>\n<pre><span><span>\u200b</span></span></pre>\n<pre><span>Of course, vertical metrics such as line height, cap height, and x-height are shared across the entire <span>*</span><span>Monospace</span><span>*</span> axis. This allows harmonious and performant layouts, even where different proportions are mixed, such as in data-rich applications and technical documentation. </span></pre>\n<pre><span><span>\u200b</span></span></pre>\n<pre><span><span>*</span><span>Recursive Sans</span><span>*</span> is made for text &amp; user interface design. While its proportional characters deliver comfortable reading at text sizes, its heaviest weights are perfect to create punchy, tightly-spaced headlines.</span></pre>\n<pre><span><span>\u200b</span></span></pre>\n<pre><span><span>*</span><span>Recursive Mono</span><span>*</span> is made for code. Its characters share the same width for clear legibility and perfect alignment. This is particularly helpful for use in programming and data-heavy design tasks, but also allows for creative possibilities in display typography.</span></pre>\n</div></div></div></div></div></div></div>\n<textarea>### A Sans for more robust layouts.\n\nThe characters within both subfamilies, Sans &amp; Mono, maintain the exact same width across all font styles, independently of the values set on the *Weight, Casual, Slant, and Cursive* axes. You can therefore use Recursive to create animated font transitions without breaking the layout of UI elements like menus and buttons.</textarea><div><div><div><div><div><div><div>\n<pre><span><span>###</span><span> A Sans for more robust layouts.</span></span></pre>\n<pre><span><span>\u200b</span></span></pre>\n<pre><span>The characters within both subfamilies, Sans &amp; Mono, maintain the exact same width across all font styles, independently of the values set on the <span>*</span><span>Weight, Casual, Slant, and Cursive</span><span>*</span> axes. You can therefore use Recursive to create animated font transitions without breaking the layout of UI elements like menus and buttons.</span></pre>\n</div></div></div></div></div></div></div>\n<textarea>## Ready for work. Ready for play. `CASL`\n\nRecursive uses its *Casual* axis (`CASL`) to offer a range of personality, allowing you to get just the right tone for any context. Along this axis, letterforms adjust in stroke curvature, contrast, and terminals to go from a sturdy, rational *Linear* to a friendly, energetic *Casual*. All the styles along this axis are designed to maintain high legibility at medium and text sizes. In display sizes, it is most effective to use either end of the *Casual* axis. \n\n*Linear* (`CASL 0`) styles have subtly-flattened edges and simple, open forms. This optimizes readability and enables enhanced focus in dense information, such as long-form text and complex code.\n\n*Casual* (`CASL 1`) echoes the soft &amp; curvy brush strokes of casual signpainting, but simplifies these forms for a striking and inviting tone. This makes it ideal for web headlines, code snippets, and command line interfaces.</textarea><div><div><div><div><div><div><div>\n<pre><span><span>##</span><span> Ready for work. Ready for play. </span><span>`</span><span>CASL</span><span>`</span></span></pre>\n<pre><span><span>\u200b</span></span></pre>\n<pre><span>Recursive uses its <span>*</span><span>Casual</span><span>*</span> axis (<span>`</span><span>CASL</span><span>`</span>) to offer a range of personality, allowing you to get just the right tone for any context. Along this axis, letterforms adjust in stroke curvature, contrast, and terminals to go from a sturdy, rational <span>*</span><span>Linear</span><span>*</span> to a friendly, energetic <span>*</span><span>Casual</span><span>*</span>. All the styles along this axis are designed to maintain high legibility at medium and text sizes. In display sizes, it is most effective to use either end of the <span>*</span><span>Casual</span><span>*</span> axis. </span></pre>\n<pre><span><span>\u200b</span></span></pre>\n<pre><span><span>*</span><span>Linear</span><span>*</span> (<span>`</span><span>CASL 0</span><span>`</span>) styles have subtly-flattened edges and simple, open forms. This optimizes readability and enables enhanced focus in dense information, such as long-form text and complex code.</span></pre>\n<pre><span><span>\u200b</span></span></pre>\n<pre><span><span>*</span><span>Casual</span><span>*</span> (<span>`</span><span>CASL 1</span><span>`</span>) echoes the soft &amp; curvy brush strokes of casual signpainting, but simplifies these forms for a striking and inviting tone. This makes it ideal for web headlines, code snippets, and command line interfaces.</span></pre>\n</div></div></div></div></div></div></div>\n<textarea>## Light to ExtraBlack. And everything in between. `wght`\n\nRecursive comes in a wide range of weights, from Light (`300`) to a super-heavy ExtraBlack (`1000`). You can choose from its seven predefined weights, or set a custom value through its *Weight* (`wght`) axis. And because Recursive maintains consistent letterforms along the entire *Weight* axis, it allows for smooth animations between any of its different weights.</textarea><div><div><div><div><div><div><div>\n<pre><span><span>##</span><span> Light to ExtraBlack. And everything in between. </span><span>`</span><span>wght</span><span>`</span></span></pre>\n<pre><span><span>\u200b</span></span></pre>\n<pre><span>Recursive comes in a wide range of weights, from Light (<span>`</span><span>300</span><span>`</span>) to a super-heavy ExtraBlack (<span>`</span><span>1000</span><span>`</span>). You can choose from its seven predefined weights, or set a custom value through its <span>*</span><span>Weight</span><span>*</span> (<span>`</span><span>wght</span><span>`</span>) axis. And because Recursive maintains consistent letterforms along the entire <span>*</span><span>Weight</span><span>*</span> axis, it allows for smooth animations between any of its different weights.</span></pre>\n</div></div></div></div></div></div></div>\n<textarea>## Slant and Cursive. Two axes that work great together, or separate. `slnt, CRSV`\n\nIn Recursive, slant and cursive letterforms can be controlled separately. The *Slant* axis (`slnt`) defines the angle of the letters, while the *Cursive* axis (`CRSV`) lets you tweak how cursive letterforms are substituted in along `slnt`.\n\nRecursive\u2019s cursive letterforms (`CRSV 1`) replace familiar \u201croman\u201d letterforms with cursive alternates like the single-story \u201ca\u201d and \u201cg\u201d. By default, Recursive will automatically apply these cursive alternates when setting the *Slant* axis (`slnt`) beyond `-14`. This allows smooth, animated transitions from normal to oblique type up to 13.99\u00b0 of slope, but also a \u201ctrue italic\u201d style with cursive letterforms at 14\u00b0. It is also possible to use sloped romans (`slnt -15, CRSV 0`), upright italics (`slnt 0, CRSV 1`), or set custom values on both axes for more options to play with.</textarea><div><div><div><div><div><div><div>\n<pre><span><span>##</span><span> Slant and Cursive. Two axes that work great together, or separate. </span><span>`</span><span>slnt, CRSV</span><span>`</span></span></pre>\n<pre><span><span>\u200b</span></span></pre>\n<pre><span>In Recursive, slant and cursive letterforms can be controlled separately. The <span>*</span><span>Slant</span><span>*</span> axis (<span>`</span><span>slnt</span><span>`</span>) defines the angle of the letters, while the <span>*</span><span>Cursive</span><span>*</span> axis (<span>`</span><span>CRSV</span><span>`</span>) lets you tweak how cursive letterforms are substituted in along <span>`</span><span>slnt</span><span>`</span>.</span></pre>\n<pre><span><span>\u200b</span></span></pre>\n<pre><span>Recursive\u2019s cursive letterforms (<span>`</span><span>CRSV 1</span><span>`</span>) replace familiar \u201croman\u201d letterforms with cursive alternates like the single-story \u201ca\u201d and \u201cg\u201d. By default, Recursive will automatically apply these cursive alternates when setting the <span>*</span><span>Slant</span><span>*</span> axis (<span>`</span><span>slnt</span><span>`</span>) beyond <span>`</span><span>-14</span><span>`</span>. This allows smooth, animated transitions from normal to oblique type up to 13.99\u00b0 of slope, but also a \u201ctrue italic\u201d style with cursive letterforms at 14\u00b0. It is also possible to use sloped romans (<span>`</span><span>slnt -15, CRSV 0</span><span>`</span>), upright italics (<span>`</span><span>slnt 0, CRSV 1</span><span>`</span>), or set custom values on both axes for more options to play with.</span></pre>\n</div></div></div></div></div></div></div>\n<textarea>## Powerful, yet simple to use.\n\nAs a variable font, Recursive gives you fine-grained control over each one of its styles. However, it also comes with 64 predefined styles that are easy to access through your font menu. Called *named instances\u00b9*, these work just like regular static fonts do.\n\n\u00b9 Named instance: a predetermined location in the designspace of a variable font, similar to the \"static instances\" that are familiar in traditional digital fonts.</textarea><div><div><div><div><div><div><div>\n<pre><span><span>##</span><span> Powerful, yet simple to use.</span></span></pre>\n<pre><span><span>\u200b</span></span></pre>\n<pre><span>As a variable font, Recursive gives you fine-grained control over each one of its styles. However, it also comes with 64 predefined styles that are easy to access through your font menu. Called <span>*</span><span>named instances\u00b9</span><span>*</span>, these work just like regular static fonts do.</span></pre>\n<pre><span><span>\u200b</span></span></pre>\n<pre><span>\u00b9 Named instance: a predetermined location in the designspace of a variable font, similar to the \"static instances\" that are familiar in traditional digital fonts.</span></pre>\n</div></div></div></div></div></div></div>\n<textarea>## Supports over 200 languages.\n\nTo meet the needs of global communication, Recursive supports a wide range of Latin-based languages, including Vietnamese. It also comes with an extended set of currencies, symbols, fractions, and arrows.</textarea><div><div><div><div><div><div><div>\n<pre><span><span>##</span><span> Supports over 200 languages.</span></span></pre>\n<pre><span><span>\u200b</span></span></pre>\n<pre><span>To meet the needs of global communication, Recursive supports a wide range of Latin-based languages, including Vietnamese. It also comes with an extended set of currencies, symbols, fractions, and arrows.</span></pre>\n</div></div></div></div></div></div></div>\n</div>\n\t\t<!-- For purge css to work it needs to see some of the codemirror classes. Maximum fun.</h2>\n\n<p>Built to maximize versatility, control, and performance, Recursive is a five-axis variable font. This enables you to choose from a wide range of predefined styles, or dial in exactly what you want for each of its axes: <em>Monospace, Casual, Weight, Slant, and Cursive</em>. Taking full advantage of variable font technology, Recursive offers an unprecedented level of flexibility, all from a single font file.ile.</p>\n\n<div>\n<input>\n<div>\n <ul>\n <li>\n <div>\n <!-- 767.98px -->\n <div>\n <span>font-size</span>: <span>12vw</span><span>;</span>\n </div>\n <!-- <div class=\"css d-md-none\">\n <span class=\"property\">font-size</span>: <span id=\"fontSizeResultSm\" contenteditable=\"true\">300px</span><span class=\"hidden--sm\">;</span>\n </div> -->\n <div>\n <span>[size]</span> <span>32vw</span><span>;</span>\n </div>\n <div>\n <input>\n </div>\n </div>\n </li>\n <!-- <li class=\"hidden--sm\"><span class=\"comment not-aligned\">&nbsp;</span></li> -->\n <li><span>/* set variation axis values */</span></li>\n <li>\n <div>\n <span><span>--mono</span><span>: </span>\"<span>MONO</span>\"\n <span>0</span><span>;</span></span>\n <span><input></span>\n <span>\n /* Monospace: Sans (natural-width) or Mono (fixed-width) */\n </span>\n </div>\n </li>\n <li>\n <div>\n <span><span>--casl</span><span>: </span>\"<span>CASL</span>\"\n <span>0</span><span>;</span></span>\n <span><input></span>\n <span>\n /* Casual: Linear to Casual */\n </span>\n </div>\n </li>\n <li>\n <div>\n <span>\n <span><span>--wght</span><span>: </span>\"<span>wght</span>\"\n <span>800</span><span>;</span></span>\n </span>\n <span><input></span>\n <span>\n /* Weight: Light to ExtraBlack; usually set with `font-weight` */\n </span>\n </div>\n </li>\n <li>\n <div>\n <span><span>--slnt</span><span>: </span>\"<span>slnt</span>\"\n <span>0</span><span>;</span></span>\n <span><input></span>\n <span>\n /* Slant: 0 to -15 degrees, auto cursive at -14 */\n </span>\n </div>\n </li>\n <li>\n <div>\n <span><span>--CRSV</span><span>: </span>\"<span>CRSV</span>\"\n <span>0.5</span><span>;</span></span>\n\n <fieldset>\n <input>\n <label>off</label>\n\n <input>\n <label>auto</label>\n\n <input>\n <label>on</label>\n </fieldset>\n <span>\n /* Cursive: always roman, auto substitution, or always cursive */\n </span>\n </div>\n </li>\n <li><span>/* apply axis values with CSS custom properties */</span></li>\n <li>\n <span>font-variation-settings</span>: <span>var</span>(<span>--mono</span>),\n <span>var</span>(<span>--casl</span>), <span>var</span>(<span>--wght</span>), <span>var</span>(<span>--slnt</span>), <span>var</span>(<span>--CRSV</span>);\n </li>\n </ul>\n</div>\n\n</div>\n\n<h2>Extraordinarily versatile.</h2>\n\n<p>Recursive draws inspiration from single-stroke casual signpainting, a style of brush writing that is stylistically flexible and warmly energetic. Adapting this aesthetic basis into a type system, Recursive is designed to excel in digital interactive environments. This makes the typeface ideal for a wide range of uses, including data-rich apps, technical documentation and code editors.</p>\n\n<p><img src=\"assets/img/mobile-app.svg\">\n<!-- <img class=\"my-4\" id=\"mobile-illustrations\" src=\"assets/img/mobile-app-angles.svg\"> --></p>\n\n<h3>One font. Infinite combinations.</h3>\n\n<p>Recursive is crafted with adaptability and diversity in mind, offering a complete type system but ensuring that each style can pair perfectly with its siblings. With so many possible variations across its subfamilies, weights and styles, Recursive allows for a dozen of font combinations that provide enough contrast to clearly define typographic roles, while maintaining a cohesive voice.</p>\n\n<h2>Sans &amp;&amp; Mono. In one file. <code>MONO</code>\n</h2>\n\n<p>The typeface comes in two practical and highly readable subfamilies, Sans and Mono. Thanks to its <em>Monospace</em> axis (<code>MONO</code>), both of these subfamilies can be used in a single font file. You can even select custom instances that are semi-proportional or semi-monospaced.</p>\n\n<p>Of course, vertical metrics such as line height, cap height, and x-height are shared across the entire <em>Monospace</em> axis. This allows harmonious and performant layouts, even where different proportions are mixed, such as in data-rich applications and technical documentation.</p>\n\n<p><em>Recursive Sans</em> is made for text &amp; user interface design. While its proportional characters deliver comfortable reading at text sizes, its heaviest weights are perfect to create punchy, tightly-spaced headlines.</p>\n\n<p><em>Recursive Mono</em> is made for code. Its characters share the same width for clear legibility and perfect alignment. This is particularly helpful for use in programming and data-heavy design tasks, but also allows for creative possibilities in display typography.</p>\n\n<h3>A Sans for more robust layouts.</h3>\n\n<p>The characters within both subfamilies, Sans &amp; Mono, maintain the exact same width across all font styles, independently of the values set on the <em>Weight, Casual, Slant, and Cursive</em> axes. You can therefore use Recursive to create animated font transitions without breaking the layout of UI elements like menus and buttons.</p>\n\n<div>\n <div>\n<ul>\n <li>Menu Item</li>\n<li>Item Two</li>\n<li>Choose Me</li>\n </ul>\n<div>font-family: <br><span>sans-serif</span>;</div>\n</div>\n<div>\n <ul>\n<li>Menu Item</li>\n<li>Item Two</li>\n<li>Choose Me</li>\n </ul>\n<div>font-family: <span>Recursive</span>;</div>\n </div>\n</div>\n\n<h2>Ready for work. Ready for play. <code>CASL</code>\n</h2>\n\n<p>Recursive uses its <em>Casual</em> axis (<code>CASL</code>) to offer a range of personality, allowing you to get just the right tone for any context. Along this axis, letterforms adjust in stroke curvature, contrast, and terminals to go from a sturdy, rational <em>Linear</em> to a friendly, energetic <em>Casual</em>. All the styles along this axis are designed to maintain high legibility at medium and text sizes. In display sizes, it is most effective to use either end of the <em>Casual</em> axis.</p>\n\n<p><em>Linear</em> (<code>CASL 0</code>) styles have subtly-flattened edges and simple, open forms. This optimizes readability and enables enhanced focus in dense information, such as long-form text and complex code.</p>\n\n<p><em>Casual</em> (<code>CASL 1</code>) echoes the soft &amp; curvy brush strokes of casual signpainting, but simplifies these forms for a striking and inviting tone. This makes it ideal for web headlines, code snippets, and command line interfaces.</p>\n\n<div>\n <div>CASL: <span>600</span>\n</div>\n <div>\n <span>&amp;</span>\n <div>\n <b>Linear</b>\n <br>1. Rationalized construction\n <br>2. Smooth counters\n <br>3. 20-unit terminal cuts\n <br>4. 20-unit inktraps\n <br>5. Flattened sides\n <br>6. Simple diagonals\n <br>7. Squared strokes\n </div>\n <div>\n <b>Casual</b>\n <br>1. Brush-based construction\n <br>2. Kinked counters\n <br>3. 6-unit inktraps &amp; terminals\n <br>4. 6-unit inktraps &amp; terminals\n <br>5. Organic curves\n <br>6. Curved diagonals\n <br>7. Softened strokes\n </div>\n </div>\n</div>\n\n<h2>Light to ExtraBlack. And everything in between. <code>wght</code>\n</h2>\n\n<p>Recursive comes in a wide range of weights, from Light (<code>300</code>) to a super-heavy Black (<code>900</code>). You can choose from its seven predefined weights, or set a custom value through its <em>Weight</em> (<code>wght</code>) axis. And because Recursive maintains consistent letterforms along the entire <em>Weight</em> axis, it allows for smooth animations between any of its different weights.</p>\n\n<div>\n <div>wght: <span>600</span>\n</div>\n <div>\n <div>CASL: 0</div>\n <div>1.00</div>\n </div>\n <div>\n <span>$</span><span>$</span><span>$</span><span>$</span><span>$</span>\n </div>\n</div>\n\n<h2>Slant and Cursive. Two axes that work great together, or separate. <code>slnt, CRSV</code>\n</h2>\n\n<p>In Recursive, slant and cursive letterforms can be controlled separately. The <em>Slant</em> axis (<code>slnt</code>) defines the angle of the letters, while the <em>Cursive</em> axis (<code>CRSV</code>) lets you tweak how cursive letterforms are substituted in along <code>slnt</code>.</p>\n\n<p>Recursive\u2019s cursive letterforms (<code>CRSV 1</code>) replace familiar \u201croman\u201d letterforms with cursive alternates like the single-story \u201ca\u201d and \u201cg\u201d. By default, Recursive will automatically apply these cursive alternates when setting the <em>Slant</em> axis (<code>slnt</code>) beyond <code>-14</code>. This allows smooth, animated transitions from normal to oblique type up to 13.99\u00b0 of slope, but also a \u201ctrue italic\u201d style with cursive letterforms at 14\u00b0. It is also possible to use sloped romans (<code>slnt -15, CRSV 0</code>), upright italics (<code>slnt 0, CRSV 1</code>), or set custom values on both axes for more options to play with.</p>\n\n<div>\n <div>slnt: <span>600</span>\n</div>\n <div>\n<span>ital: 0 (off)</span><span>ital: 0.5 (auto)</span><span>ital: 1 (on)</span>\n</div>\n <div>\n<span>\u200ag\u200a</span><span>\u200ag\u200a</span><span>\u200ag\u200a</span>\n</div>\n</div>\n\n<h2>Powerful, yet simple to use.</h2>\n\n<p>As a variable font, Recursive gives you fine-grained control over each one of its styles. However, it also comes with 64 predefined styles that are easy to access through your font menu. Called <em>named instances\u00b9</em>, these work just like regular static fonts do.</p>\n\n<p>\u00b9 Named instance: a predetermined location in the designspace of a variable font, similar to the \u201cstatic instances\u201d that are familiar in traditional digital fonts.</p>\n\n<div>\n <div>\n <div>\n <div>\n Recursive\n </div>\n <div>\n <div>Light<br><span>(300)</span>\n</div>\n <div>ExtraBold<br><span>(800)</span>\n</div>\n <div>Heavy<br><span>(900)</span>\n</div>\n <div>ExtraBlack<br><span>(1000)</span>\n</div>\n </div>\n </div>\n <div>\n <div>\n <div>\n <div>Mono</div>\n Recursive supports a wide range of Latin-based languages, including Vietnamese. It also comes with an extended set of currencies, symbols, fractions, and arrows.</p>\n\n<div>\n <div>\n <span>\n Abenaki, Afaan Oromo, Afar, Afrikaans, Albanian, Alsatian, Amis, Anuta, Aragonese, "raw_markdown": "[ Recursive Sans & Mono ](https://www.recursive.design/)\n * [Features](https://www.recursive.design/#toolbar)\n * [Process](https://www.recursive.design/process)\n * [PDF (11MB)](https://www.recursive.design/assets/arrowtype-recursive-sansmono-specimen-230407.pdf)\n * [Source \u2197 ](https://github.com/arrowtype/recursive/)\n\n\nGet Recursive \n## Get Recursive\n[Download \u2193](https://github.com/arrowtype/recursive/releases/download/v1.085/ArrowType-Recursive-1.085.zip)\n### Webfonts from Google Fonts\nGet the [partial family on Google Fonts](https://fonts.google.com/specimen/Recursive) or the full family via the Google Fonts API, configurable with the controls below.\n#### Configure\n##### Monospace\nValue Range\n0\n1\n0\n##### Casual\nValue Range\n0\n1\n0\n##### Weight\nValue Range\n300\n800\n1000\n400\n##### Slant\nValue Range\n-15\n0\n0\n##### Cursive\nValue Range\n0\n1\n0.5\n#### Filesize\n\u224827kb 281kb\nEstimated size of woff2 file with a basic Latin character set. Actual results may vary.\n#### Embed\nTo embed Recursive into a webpage, copy this code into the <head> of your HTML.\nHTML Link CSS Import\n`     <link href=\"https://fonts.googleapis.com/css2?family=Recursive&display=swap\"     rel=\"stylesheet\">     `\nCSS declaration to specify Recursive:\n`font-family: 'Recursive', monospace;`\nVisit the [Google Fonts API Docs](https://developers.google.com/fonts/docs/css2) to learn more about custom font requests.\nWeight\nCasual\nSlant\nA typographic palette for vibrant code & UI \n[Custom Styles] Default Styles Mono Casual Light Mono Casual Light Italic Mono Casual Regular Mono Casual Italic Mono Casual Medium Mono Casual Medium Italic Mono Casual SemiBold Mono Casual SemiBold Italic Mono Casual Bold Mono Casual Bold Italic Mono Casual ExtraBold Mono Casual ExtraBold Italic Mono Casual Black Mono Casual Black Italic Mono Casual ExtraBlack Mono Casual ExtraBlack Italic Mono Linear Light Mono Linear Light Italic Mono Linear Regular Mono Linear Italic Mono Linear Medium Mono Linear Medium Italic Mono Linear SemiBold Mono Linear SemiBold Italic Mono Linear Bold Mono Linear Bold Italic Mono Linear Sans Casual Italic Sans Casual Medium Sans Casual Medium Italic Sans Casual SemiBold Sans Casual SemiBold Italic Sans Casual Bold Sans Casual Bold Italic Sans Casual ExtraBold Sans Casual ExtraBold
