Medium Sans Linear Medium Italic Sans Linear SemiBold Sans Linear SemiBold Italic Sans Linear Bold Sans Linear Bold Italic Sans Linear ExtraBold Sans Linear ExtraBold Italic Sans Linear Black Sans Linear Black Italic Sans Linear ExtraBlack Sans Linear ExtraBlack Italic\n15pt \n * \n\nMONO 0.00 CASL 0.00 wght 400 slnt 0.00 CRSV 0\n * MONO\n * CASL\n * wght\n * slnt\n * CRSV\n\n\n## Maximum utility. Maximum fun. Built to maximize versatility, control, and performance, Recursive is a five-axis variable font. This enables you to choose from a wide range of predefined styles, or dial in exactly what you want for each of its axes: *Monospace, Casual, Weight, Slant, and Cursive*. Taking full advantage of variable font technology, Recursive offers an unprecedented level of flexibility, all from a single font file.\n`\n## Maximum utility. Maximum fun.\n`\n`\n\u200b\n`\n`\nBuilt to maximize versatility, control, and performance, Recursive is a five-axis variable font. This enables you to choose from a wide range of predefined styles, or dial in exactly what you want for each of its axes: *Monospace, Casual, Weight, Slant, and Cursive*. Taking full advantage of variable font technology, Recursive offers an unprecedented level of flexibility, all from a single font file.\n`\n\n## Extraordinarily versatile. Recursive draws inspiration from single-stroke casual signpainting, a style of brush writing that is stylistically flexible and warmly energetic. Adapting this aesthetic basis into a type system, Recursive is designed to excel in digital interactive environments. This makes the typeface ideal for a wide range of uses, including data-rich apps, technical documentation and code editors.\n`\n## Extraordinarily versatile.\n`\n`\n\u200b\n`\n`\nRecursive draws inspiration from single-stroke casual signpainting, a style of brush writing that is stylistically flexible and warmly energetic. Adapting this aesthetic basis into a type system, Recursive is designed to excel in digital interactive environments. This makes the typeface ideal for a wide range of uses, including data-rich apps, technical documentation and code editors.\n`\n\n### One font. Infinite combinations. Recursive is crafted with adaptability and diversity in mind, offering a complete type system but ensuring that each style can pair perfectly with its siblings. With so many possible variations across its subfamilies, weights and styles, Recursive allows for a dozen of font combinations that provide enough contrast to clearly define typographic roles, while maintaining a cohesive voice. ## Sans && Mono. In one file. `MONO` The typeface comes in two practical and highly readable subfamilies, Sans and Mono. Thanks to its *Monospace* axis (`MONO`), both of these subfamilies can be used in a single font file. You can even select custom instances that are semi-proportional or semi-monospaced. Of course, vertical metrics such as line height, cap height, and x-height are shared across the entire *Monospace* axis. This allows harmonious and performant layouts, even where different proportions are mixed, such as in data-rich applications and technical documentation. *Recursive Sans* is made for text & user interface design. While its proportional characters deliver comfortable reading at text sizes, its heaviest weights are perfect to create punchy, tightly-spaced headlines. *Recursive Mono* is made for code. Its characters share the same width for clear legibility and perfect alignment. This is particularly helpful for use in programming and data-heavy design tasks, but also allows for creative possibilities in display typography.\n`\n### One font. Infinite combinations.\n`\n`\n\u200b\n`\n`\nRecursive is crafted with adaptability and diversity in mind, offering a complete type system but ensuring that each style can pair perfectly with its siblings. With so many possible variations across its subfamilies, weights and styles, Recursive allows for a dozen of font combinations that provide enough contrast to clearly define typographic roles, while maintaining a cohesive voice.\n`\n`\n\u200b\n`\n`\n\u200b\n`\n``\n## Sans && Mono. In one file. `MONO`\n``\n`\n\u200b\n`\n``\nThe typeface comes in two practical and highly readable subfamilies, Sans and Mono. Thanks to its *Monospace* axis (`MONO`), both of these subfamilies can be used in a single font file. You can even select custom instances that are semi-proportional or semi-monospaced. \n``\n`\n\u200b\n`\n`\nOf course, vertical metrics such as line height, cap height, and x-height are shared across the entire *Monospace* axis. This allows harmonious and performant layouts, even where different proportions are mixed, such as in data-rich applications and technical documentation. \n`\n`\n\u200b\n`\n`\n*Recursive Sans* is made for text & user interface design. While its proportional characters deliver comfortable reading at text sizes, its heaviest weights are perfect to create punchy, tightly-spaced headlines.\n`\n`\n\u200b\n`\n`\n*Recursive Mono* is made for code. Its characters share the same width for clear legibility and perfect alignment. This is particularly helpful for use in programming and data-heavy design tasks, but also allows for creative possibilities in display typography.\n`\n\n### A Sans for more robust layouts. The characters within both subfamilies, Sans & Mono, maintain the exact same width across all font styles, independently of the values set on the *Weight, Casual, Slant, and Cursive* axes. You can therefore use Recursive to create animated font transitions without breaking the layout of UI elements like menus and buttons.\n`\n### A Sans for more robust layouts.\n`\n`\n\u200b\n`\n`\nThe characters within both subfamilies, Sans & Mono, maintain the exact same width across all font styles, independently of the values set on the *Weight, Casual, Slant, and Cursive* axes. You can therefore use Recursive to create animated font transitions without breaking the layout of UI elements like menus and buttons.\n`\n\n## Ready for work. Ready for play. `CASL` Recursive uses its *Casual* axis (`CASL`) to offer a range of personality, allowing you to get just the right tone for any context. Along this axis, letterforms adjust in stroke curvature, contrast, and terminals to go from a sturdy, rational *Linear* to a friendly, energetic *Casual*. All the styles along this axis are designed to maintain high legibility at medium and text sizes. In display sizes, it is most effective to use either end of the *Casual* axis. *Linear* (`CASL 0`) styles have subtly-flattened edges and simple, open forms. This optimizes readability and enables enhanced focus in dense information, such as long-form text and complex code. *Casual* (`CASL 1`) echoes the soft & curvy brush strokes of casual signpainting, but simplifies these forms for a striking and inviting tone. This makes it ideal for web headlines, code snippets, and command line interfaces.\n``\n## Ready for work. Ready for play. `CASL`\n``\n`\n\u200b\n`\n``\nRecursive uses its *Casual* axis (`CASL`) to offer a range of personality, allowing you to get just the right tone for any context. Along this axis, letterforms adjust in stroke curvature, contrast, and terminals to go from a sturdy, rational *Linear* to a friendly, energetic *Casual*. All the styles along this axis are designed to maintain high legibility at medium and text sizes. In display sizes, it is most effective to use either end of the *Casual* axis. \n``\n`\n\u200b\n`\n``\n*Linear* (`CASL 0`) styles have subtly-flattened edges and simple, open forms. This optimizes readability and enables enhanced focus in dense information, such as long-form text and complex code.\n``\n`\n\u200b\n`\n``\n*Casual* (`CASL 1`) echoes the soft & curvy brush strokes of casual signpainting, but simplifies these forms for a striking and inviting tone. This makes it ideal for web headlines, code snippets, and command line interfaces.\n``\n\n## Light to ExtraBlack. And everything in between. `wght` Recursive comes in a wide range of weights, from Light (`300`) to a super-heavy ExtraBlack (`1000`). You can choose from its seven predefined weights, or set a custom value through its *Weight* (`wght`) axis. And because Recursive maintains consistent letterforms along the entire *Weight* axis, it allows for smooth animations between any of its different weights.\n``\n## Light to ExtraBlack. And everything in between. `wght`\n``\n`\n\u200b\n`\n``\nRecursive comes in a wide range of weights, from Light (`300`) to a super-heavy ExtraBlack (`1000`). You can choose from its seven predefined weights, or set a custom value through its *Weight* (`wght`) axis. And because Recursive maintains consistent letterforms along the entire *Weight* axis, it allows for smooth animations between any of its different weights.\n``\n\n## Slant and Cursive. Two axes that work great together, or separate. `slnt, CRSV` In Recursive, slant and cursive letterforms can be controlled separately. The *Slant* axis (`slnt`) defines the angle of the letters, while the *Cursive* axis (`CRSV`) lets you tweak how cursive letterforms are substituted in along `slnt`. Recursive\u2019s cursive letterforms (`CRSV 1`) replace familiar \u201croman\u201d letterforms with cursive alternates like the single-story \u201ca\u201d and \u201cg\u201d. By default, Recursive will automatically apply these cursive alternates when setting the *Slant* axis (`slnt`) beyond `-14`. This allows smooth, animated transitions from normal to oblique type up to 13.99\u00b0 of slope, but also a \u201ctrue italic\u201d style with cursive letterforms at 14\u00b0. It is also possible to use sloped romans (`slnt -15, CRSV 0`), upright italics (`slnt 0, CRSV 1`), or set custom values on both axes for more options to play with.\n``\n## Slant and Cursive. Two axes that work great together, or separate. `slnt, CRSV`\n``\n`\n\u200b\n`\n``\nIn Recursive, slant and cursive letterforms can be controlled separately. The *Slant* axis (`slnt`) defines the angle of the letters, while the *Cursive* axis (`CRSV`) lets you tweak how cursive letterforms are substituted in along `slnt`.\n``\n`\n\u200b\n`\n``\nRecursive\u2019s cursive letterforms (`CRSV 1`) replace familiar \u201croman\u201d letterforms with cursive alternates like the single-story \u201ca\u201d and \u201cg\u201d. By default, Recursive will automatically apply these cursive alternates when setting the *Slant* axis (`slnt`) beyond `-14`. This allows smooth, animated transitions from normal to oblique type up to 13.99\u00b0 of slope, but also a \u201ctrue italic\u201d style with cursive letterforms at 14\u00b0. It is also possible to use sloped romans (`slnt -15, CRSV 0`), upright italics (`slnt 0, CRSV 1`), or set custom values on both axes for more options to play with.\n``\n\n## Powerful, yet simple to use. As a variable font, Recursive gives you fine-grained control over each one of its styles. However, it also comes with 64 predefined styles that are easy to access through your font menu. Called *named instances\u00b9*, these work just like regular static fonts do. \u00b9 Named instance: a predetermined location in the designspace of a variable font, similar to the \"static instances\" that are familiar in traditional digital fonts.\n`\n## Powerful, yet simple to use.\n`\n`\n\u200b\n`\n`\nAs a variable font, Recursive gives you fine-grained control over each one of its styles. However, it also comes with 64 predefined styles that are easy to access through your font menu. Called *named instances\u00b9*, these work just like regular static fonts do.\n`\n`\n\u200b\n`\n`\n\u00b9 Named instance: a predetermined location in the designspace of a variable font, similar to the \"static instances\" that are familiar in traditional digital fonts.\n`\n\n## Supports over 200 languages. To meet the needs of global communication, Recursive supports a wide range of Latin-based languages, including Vietnamese. It also comes with an extended set of currencies, symbols, fractions, and arrows.\n`\n## Supports over 200 languages.\n`\n`\n\u200b\n`\n`\nTo meet the needs of global communication, Recursive supports a wide range of Latin-based languages, including Vietnamese. It also comes with an extended set of currencies, symbols, fractions, and arrows.\n`\n\n## Maximum utility. Maximum fun.\nBuilt to maximize versatility, control, and performance, Recursive is a five-axis variable font. This enables you to choose from a wide range of predefined styles, or dial in exactly what you want for each of its axes: \_Monospace, Casual, Weight, Slant, and Cursive_. Taking full advantage of variable font technology, Recursive offers an unprecedented level of flexibility, all from a single font file.ile.\n _ font-size: 12vw;\n[size] 32vw;\n _ /_ set variation axis values _/\n _ --mono: \"MONO\" 0; /_ Monospace: Sans (natural-width) or Mono (fixed-width) _/ \n _ --casl: \"CASL\" 0; /_ Casual: Linear to Casual _/ \n _ --wght: \"wght\" 800; /_ Weight: Light to ExtraBlack; usually set with `font-weight` _/ \n _ --slnt: \"slnt\" 0; /_ Slant: 0 to -15 degrees, auto cursive at -14 _/ \n _ --CRSV: \"CRSV\" 0.5; off auto on /_ Cursive: always roman, auto substitution, or always cursive _/ \n _ /_ apply axis values with CSS custom properties _/\n _ font-variation-settings: var(--mono), var(--casl), var(--wght), var(--slnt), var(--CRSV); \n\n\n## Extraordinarily versatile.\nRecursive draws inspiration from single-stroke casual signpainting, a style of brush writing that is stylistically flexible and warmly energetic. Adapting this aesthetic basis into a type system, Recursive is designed to excel in digital interactive environments. This makes the typeface ideal for a wide range of uses, including data-rich apps, technical documentation and code editors.\n![](https://www.recursive.design/assets/img/mobile-app.svg)\n### One font. Infinite combinations.\nRecursive is crafted with adaptability and diversity in mind, offering a complete type system but ensuring that each style can pair perfectly with its siblings. With so many possible variations across its subfamilies, weights and styles, Recursive allows for a dozen of font combinations that provide enough contrast to clearly define typographic roles, while maintaining a cohesive voice.\n## Sans && Mono. In one file. `MONO`\nThe typeface comes in two practical and highly readable subfamilies, Sans and Mono. Thanks to its *Monospace* axis (`MONO`), both of these subfamilies can be used in a single font file. You can even select custom instances that are semi-proportional or semi-monospaced.\nOf course, vertical metrics such as line height, cap height, and x-height are shared across the entire *Monospace* axis. This allows harmonious and performant layouts, even where different proportions are mixed, such as in data-rich applications and technical documentation.\n*Recursive Sans* is made for text & user interface design. While its proportional characters deliver comfortable reading at text sizes, its heaviest weights are perfect to create punchy, tightly-spaced headlines.\n*Recursive Mono* is made for code. Its characters share the same width for clear legibility and perfect alignment. This is particularly helpful for use in programming and data-heavy design tasks, but also allows for creative possibilities in display typography.\n### A Sans for more robust layouts.\nThe characters within both subfamilies, Sans & Mono, maintain the exact same width across all font styles, independently of the values set on the *Weight, Casual, Slant, and Cursive* axes. You can therefore use Recursive to create animated font transitions without breaking the layout of UI elements like menus and buttons.\n _ Menu Item\n _ Item Two\n _ Choose Me\n\n\nfont-family: \nsans-serif;\n _ Menu Item\n _ Item Two\n _ Choose Me\n\n\nfont-family: Recursive;\n## Ready for work. Ready for play. `CASL`\nRecursive uses its *Casual* axis (`CASL`) to offer a range of personality, allowing you to get just the right tone for any context. Along this axis, letterforms adjust in stroke curvature, contrast, and terminals to go from a sturdy, rational *Linear* to a friendly, energetic *Casual*. All the styles along this axis are designed to maintain high legibility at medium and text sizes. In display sizes, it is most effective to use either end of the *Casual* axis.\n*Linear* (`CASL 0`) styles have subtly-flattened edges and simple, open forms. This optimizes readability and enables enhanced focus in dense information, such as long-form text and complex code.\n*Casual* (`CASL 1`) echoes the soft & curvy brush strokes of casual signpainting, but simplifies these forms for a striking and inviting tone. This makes it ideal for web headlines, code snippets, and command line interfaces.\nCASL: 600\n&\n**Linear** \n1. Rationalized construction \n2. Smooth counters \n3. 20-unit terminal cuts \n4. 20-unit inktraps \n5. Flattened sides \n6. Simple diagonals \n7. Squared strokes \n**Casual** \n1. Brush-based construction \n2. Kinked counters \n3. 6-unit inktraps & terminals \n4. 6-unit inktraps & terminals \n5. Organic curves \n6. Curved diagonals \n7. Softened strokes \n## Light to ExtraBlack. And everything in between. `wght`\nRecursive comes in a wide range of weights, from Light (`300`) to a super-heavy Black (`900`). You can choose from its seven predefined weights, or set a custom value through its *Weight* (`wght`) axis. And because Recursive maintains consistent letterforms along the entire *Weight* axis, it allows for smooth animations between any of its different weights.\nwght: 600\nCASL: 0\n1.00\n$$$$$\n## Slant and Cursive. Maximum fun. Built to maximize versatility, control, and performance, Recursive is a five-axis variable font. This enables you to choose from a wide range of predefined styles, or dial in exactly what you want for each of its axes: *Monospace, Casual, Weight, Slant, and Cursive*. Taking full advantage of variable font technology, Recursive offers an unprecedented level of flexibility, all from a single font file.\n`\n## Maximum utility. Maximum fun.\n`\n`\n\u200b\n`\n```\nBuilt to maximize versatility, control, and performance, Recursive is a five-axis variable font. This enables you to choose from a wide range of predefined styles, or dial in exactly what you want for each of its axes: *Monospace, Casual, Weight, Slant, and Cursive*. Taking full advantage of variable font technology, Recursive offers an unprecedented level of flexibility, all from a single font file.\n`\n\n## Extraordinarily versatile. Recursive draws inspiration from single-stroke casual signpainting, a style of brush writing that is stylistically flexible and warmly energetic. Adapting this aesthetic basis into a type system, Recursive is designed to excel in digital interactive environments. This makes the typeface ideal for a wide range of uses, including data-rich apps, technical documentation and code editors.\n`\n## Extraordinarily versatile.\n`\n`\n\u200b\n`\n`\nRecursive draws inspiration from single-stroke casual signpainting, a style of brush writing that is stylistically flexible and warmly energetic. Adapting this aesthetic basis into a type system, Recursive is designed to excel in digital interactive environments. This makes the typeface ideal for a wide range of uses, including data-rich apps, technical documentation and code editors.\n```\n\n### One font. Infinite combinations. Recursive is crafted with adaptability and diversity in mind, offering a complete type system but ensuring that each style can pair perfectly with its siblings. With so many possible variations across its subfamilies, weights and styles, Recursive allows for a dozen of font combinations that provide enough contrast to clearly define typographic roles, while maintaining a cohesive voice. ## Sans && Mono. In one file. `MONO` The typeface comes in two practical and highly readable subfamilies, Sans and Mono. Thanks to its *Monospace* axis (`MONO`), both of these subfamilies can be used in a single font file. You can even select custom instances that are semi-proportional or semi-monospaced. Of course, vertical metrics such as line height, cap height, and x-height are shared across the entire *Monospace* axis. This allows harmonious and performant layouts, even where different proportions are mixed, such as in data-rich applications and technical documentation. *Recursive Sans* is made for text & user interface design. While its proportional characters deliver comfortable reading at text sizes, its heaviest weights are perfect to create punchy, tightly-spaced headlines. *Recursive Mono* is made for code. Its characters share the same width for clear legibility and perfect alignment. This is particularly helpful for use in programming and data-heavy design tasks, but also allows for creative possibilities in display typography.\n`\n### One font. Infinite combinations.\n`\n`\n\u200b\n`\n`\nRecursive is crafted with adaptability and diversity in mind, offering a complete type system but ensuring that each style can pair perfectly with its siblings. With so many possible variations across its subfamilies, weights and styles, Recursive allows for a dozen of font combinations that provide enough contrast to clearly define typographic roles, while maintaining a cohesive voice.\n`\n`\n\u200b\n`\n`\n\u200b\n`\n``\n## Sans && Mono. In one file. `MONO`\n``\n`\n\u200b\n`\n```\nThe typeface comes in two practical and highly readable subfamilies, Sans and Mono. Thanks to its *Monospace* axis (`MONO`), both of these subfamilies can be used in a single font file. You can even select custom instances that are semi-proportional or semi-monospaced. \n`\n`\n\u200b\n`\n`\nOf course, vertical metrics such as line height, cap height, and x-height are shared across the entire *Monospace* axis. This allows harmonious and performant layouts, even where different proportions are mixed, such as in data-rich applications and technical documentation. \n`\n`\n\u200b\n`\n`\n*Recursive Sans* is made for text & user interface design. While its proportional characters deliver comfortable reading at text sizes, its heaviest weights are perfect to create punchy, tightly-spaced headlines.\n`\n`\n\u200b\n`\n`\n*Recursive Mono* is made for code. Its characters share the same width for clear legibility and perfect alignment. This is particularly helpful for use in programming and data-heavy design tasks, but also allows for creative possibilities in display typography.\n```\n\n### A Sans for more robust layouts. The characters within both subfamilies, Sans & Mono, maintain the exact same width across all font styles, independently of the values set on the *Weight, Casual, Slant, and Cursive* axes. You can therefore use Recursive to create animated font transitions without breaking the layout of UI elements like menus and buttons.\n`\n### A Sans for more robust layouts.\n`\n`\n\u200b\n`\n```\nThe characters within both subfamilies, Sans & Mono, maintain the exact same width across all font styles, independently of the values set on the *Weight, Casual, Slant, and Cursive* axes. You can therefore use Recursive to create animated font transitions without breaking the layout of UI elements like menus and buttons.\n```\n\n## Ready for work. Ready for play. `CASL` Recursive uses its *Casual* axis (`CASL`) to offer a range of personality, allowing you to get just the right tone for any context. Along this axis, letterforms adjust in stroke curvature, contrast, and terminals to go from a sturdy, rational *Linear* to a friendly, energetic *Casual*. All the styles along this axis are designed to maintain high legibility at medium and text sizes. In display sizes, it is most effective to use either end of the *Casual* axis. *Linear* (`CASL 0`) styles have subtly-flattened edges and simple, open forms. This optimizes readability and enables enhanced focus in dense information, such as long-form text and complex code. *Casual* (`CASL 1`) echoes the soft & curvy brush strokes of casual signpainting, but simplifies these forms for a striking and inviting tone. This makes it ideal for web headlines, code snippets, and command line interfaces.\n``\n## Ready for work. Ready for play. `CASL`\n``\n`\n\u200b\n`\n```\nRecursive uses its *Casual* axis (`CASL`) to offer a range of personality, allowing you to get just the right tone for any context. Along this axis, letterforms adjust in stroke curvature, contrast, and terminals to go from a sturdy, rational *Linear* to a friendly, energetic *Casual*. All the styles along this axis are designed to maintain high legibility at medium and text sizes. In display sizes, it is most effective to use either end of the *Casual* axis. \n`\n`\n\u200b\n`\n`\n*Linear* (`CASL 0`) styles have subtly-flattened edges and simple, open forms. This optimizes readability and enables enhanced focus in dense information, such as long-form text and complex code.\n`\n`\n\u200b\n`\n`\n*Casual* (`CASL 1`) echoes the soft & curvy brush strokes of casual signpainting, but simplifies these forms for a striking and inviting tone. This makes it ideal for web headlines, code snippets, and command line interfaces.\n```\n\n## Light to ExtraBlack. And everything in between. `wght` Recursive comes in a wide range of weights, from Light (`300`) to a super-heavy ExtraBlack (`1000`). You can choose from its seven predefined weights, or set a custom value through its *Weight* (`wght`) axis. And because Recursive maintains consistent letterforms along the entire *Weight* axis, it allows for smooth animations between any of its different weights.\n``\n## Light to ExtraBlack. And everything in between. `wght`\n``\n`\n\u200b\n`\n```\nRecursive comes in a wide range of weights, from Light (`300`) to a super-heavy ExtraBlack (`1000`). You can choose from its seven predefined weights, or set a custom value through its *Weight* (`wght`) axis. And because Recursive maintains consistent letterforms along the entire *Weight* axis, it allows for smooth animations between any of its different weights.\n```\n\n## Slant and Cursive. Two axes that work great together, or separate. `slnt, CRSV` In Recursive, slant and cursive letterforms can be controlled separately. The *Slant* axis (`slnt`) defines the angle of the letters, while the *Cursive* axis (`CRSV`) lets you tweak how cursive letterforms are substituted in along `slnt`. Recursive\u2019s cursive letterforms (`CRSV 1`) replace familiar \u201croman\u201d letterforms with cursive alternates like the single-story \u201ca\u201d and \u201cg\u201d. By default, Recursive will automatically apply these cursive alternates when setting the *Slant* axis (`slnt`) beyond `-14`. This allows smooth, animated transitions from normal to oblique type up to 13.99\u00b0 of slope, but also a \u201ctrue italic\u201d style with cursive letterforms at 14\u00b0. It is also possible to use sloped romans (`slnt -15, CRSV 0`), upright italics (`slnt 0, CRSV 1`), or set custom values on both axes for more options to play with.\n``\n## Slant and Cursive. Two axes that work great together, or separate. `slnt, CRSV`\n``\n`\n\u200b\n`\n```\nIn Recursive, slant and cursive letterforms can be controlled separately. The *Slant* axis (`slnt`) defines the angle of the letters, while the *Cursive* axis (`CRSV`) lets you tweak how cursive letterforms are substituted in along `slnt`.\n`\n`\n\u200b\n`\n`\nRecursive\u2019s cursive letterforms (`CRSV 1`) replace familiar \u201croman\u201d letterforms with cursive alternates like the single-story \u201ca\u201d and \u201cg\u201d. By default, Recursive will automatically apply these cursive alternates when setting the *Slant* axis (`slnt`) beyond `-14`. This allows smooth, animated transitions from normal to oblique type up to 13.99\u00b0 of slope, but also a \u201ctrue italic\u201d style with cursive letterforms at 14\u00b0. It is also possible to use sloped romans (`slnt -15, CRSV 0`), upright italics (`slnt 0, CRSV 1`), or set custom values on both axes for more options to play with.\n```\n\n## Powerful, yet simple to use. As a variable font, Recursive gives you fine-grained control over each one of its styles. However, it also comes with 64 predefined styles that are easy to access through your font menu. Called *named instances\u00b9*, these work just like regular static fonts do. \u00b9 Named instance: a predetermined location in the designspace of a variable font, similar to the \"static instances\" that are familiar in traditional digital fonts.\n`\n## Powerful, yet simple to use.\n`\n`\n\u200b\n`\n```\nAs a variable font, Recursive gives you fine-grained control over each one of its styles. However, it also comes with 64 predefined styles that are easy to access through your font menu. Called *named instances\u00b9*, these work just like regular static fonts do.\n`\n`\n\u200b\n`\n`\n\u00b9 Named instance: a predetermined location in the designspace of a variable font, similar to the \"static instances\" that are familiar in traditional digital fonts.\n`\n\n## Supports over 200 languages. To meet the needs of global communication, Recursive supports a wide range of Latin-based languages, including Vietnamese. It also comes with an extended set of currencies, symbols, fractions, and arrows.\n`\n## Supports over 200 languages.\n`\n`\n\u200b\n`\n`\nTo meet the needs of global communication, Recursive supports a wide range of Latin-based languages, including Vietnamese. It also comes with an extended set of currencies, symbols, fractions, and arrows.\n```\n\n## Maximum utility. Maximum fun.\nBuilt to maximize versatility, control, and performance, Recursive is a five-axis variable font. This enables you to choose from a wide range of predefined styles, or dial in exactly what you want for each of its axes: *Monospace, Casual, Weight, Slant, and Cursive*. Taking full advantage of variable font technology, Recursive offers an unprecedented level of flexibility, all from a single font file.ile.\n * font-size: 12vw;\n[size] 32vw;\n _ /_ set variation axis values _/\n _ --mono: \"MONO\" 0; /_ Monospace: Sans (natural-width) or Mono (fixed-width) _/ \n _ --casl: \"CASL\" 0; /_ Casual: Linear to Casual _/ \n _ --wght: \"wght\" 800; /_ Weight: Light to ExtraBlack; usually set with `font-weight` _/ \n _ --slnt: \"slnt\" 0; /_ Slant: 0 to -15 degrees, auto cursive at -14 _/ \n _ --CRSV: \"CRSV\" 0.5; off auto on /_ Cursive: always roman, auto substitution, or always cursive _/ \n _ /_ apply axis values with CSS custom properties _/\n _ font-variation-settings: var(--mono), var(--casl), var(--wght), var(--slnt), var(--CRSV); \n\n\n## Extraordinarily versatile.\nRecursive draws inspiration from single-stroke casual signpainting, a style of brush writing that is stylistically flexible and warmly energetic. Adapting this aesthetic basis into a type system, Recursive is designed to excel in digital interactive environments.
